In re J.D.W.B.


Civ. No. 26474


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Four


8 Cal. App. 3d 103; 87 Cal. Rptr. 178; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 2025



May 26, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied July 22, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Santa Clara County, Homer B. Thompson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order appealed from is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile appealed the order of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California) granting application of appellee Youth Authority Board for juvenile's continued detention.


OVERVIEW: Appellee Youth Authority Board petitioned for the continued detention of appellant juvenile based on claim that juvenile's release at the ordinarily applicable time would be physically dangerous to the public. The petition was granted. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the validity of extended control under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 1800 et seq. depended in part on the validity of the original commitment. The court further held that the original commitment proceedings were deficient due to a lack of counsel for the juvenile, lack of explanation of the nature of the charge, self-incrimination, absence of confrontation, absence of intelligent waiver, and failure to advise of the consequences of the minor's assent to the charge.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court, holding that continued detention of appellant juvenile could not occur where juvenile's original commitment proceeding lacked numerous due process protections.

 

1033 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Greenberg v. Hollywood Turf Club


Civ. No. 33917


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


7 Cal. App. 3d 968; 86 Cal. Rptr. 885; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 2227



May 22, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Clinton Rodda, Temporary Judge. *


* Pursuant to Constitution, article VI, section 21.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed with respect to the respondent Board and respondents Hills, Kornick and Fluor. The judgment is also affirmed with respect to the respondent Stewart as to counts I and II. The judgment is reversed with respect to the respondent Hollywood as to counts I, II, IV and V and with respect to the respondent Stewart as to counts IV and V.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff horse trainer sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which sustained the demurrers of six of the defendants in plaintiff's suit against them for various causes of action relating to his exclusion from a race track stable area.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff horse trainer brought suit against defendants, race track operator and its agent, horse racing board and its members, and others, alleging various causes of action. The causes of action resulted from plaintiff's exclusion from the stable area of a race track. Some of the defendant's countered with demurrers, which were sustained by the trial court with leave to amend. Plaintiff failed to amend and appealed. The court affirmed with respect to defendants, horse racing board and its members. The court affirmed as to defendant race track operator's agent, and reversed as to defendant race track operator, as to the counts pertaining to the constitutionality of the exclusion from the stable area. The court reversed as to defendant's race track operator and its agent, with respect to the counts for inducement of breach of employment contract and for intentionally interfering with plaintiff's prospective economic advantage, holding that a party whose conduct causes legal injury should have to justify the exclusion of trainers or stable agents from the few places where they could apply their trade or find future employment.


OUTCOME: The court held that the judgment was affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that the trial court erred in sustaining the demurrers of defendants, race track operator and its agent, regarding horse trainer's allegation of interference with plaintiff's prospective advantage because they should have had to justify the exclusion of trainers from the few places where they could ply their trade or find future employment.

 

1034 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


In re Joseph G.


Civ. Nos. 1119, 1120, 1121


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


7 Cal. App. 3d 695; 87 Cal. Rptr. 25; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 2207



May 18, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied July 16, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Merced County, Donald R. Fretz and Howard C. George, Judges.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juveniles sought review of a judgment from the Juvenile Department of the Superior Court of Merced County (California), which found them to come within the provisions of Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 602 by reason of having violated Cal. Penal Code § 647(f), disorderly conduct by being under the influence of intoxicating liquor. Appellants were adjudged wards of the court and placed on probation.


OVERVIEW: Appellant juveniles were adjudged wards of the juvenile court and placed on probation after the juvenile court found them to come within the provisions of Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 602 by reason of having violated Cal. Penal Code § 647(f), disorderly conduct by being under the influence of intoxicating liquor. On appeal, the court found impropriety in the fact that the probation officer's opinion of appellants' guilt was incorporated into the jurisdictional report, but held that the impropriety was of less than reversible dimensions. The court also rejected appellants' argument that the use of the word "safety" in § 647(f) was unconstitutionally vague. Nevertheless, the court reversed the judgment of the juvenile court on the ground that appellants' guilt was not proved beyond a reasonable doubt. The court assumed that the juvenile court followed the state law at the time of trial, which required proof by a preponderance of the evidence. However, a subsequent United States Supreme Court ruling required proof beyond a reasonable doubt, and the court held that the new standard was applicable to cases pending on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment that adjudged appellant juveniles wards of the juvenile court after they were found guilty of disorderly conduct by being under the influence of intoxicating liquor. Appellants were denied a constitutional right because their guilt was determined by a preponderance of evidence standard rather than by the standard of proof beyond a reasonable doubt.

 

1035 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Mihans v. Municipal Court


Civ. No. 27931


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


7 Cal. App. 3d 479; 87 Cal. Rptr. 17; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 2181



May 11, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The petition is dismissed as to petitioners Mihans and Akers. The peremptory writ is granted as to the other petitioners.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners challenged a judgment from the Superior Court, Alameda County (California), in a landlord-tenant action where the appeals court had denied petitioners' request for a writ of prohibition to preclude the trial court from granting the real party in interest immediate possession of the premises in questions, in cases where petitioner tenants were insolvent.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners were tenants in possession of premises. In the trial court the real party in interest filed a verified complaint in unlawful detainer seeking restitution of the premises. Petitioners contended that Cal. Civ. Proc. Code 1166a was unconstitutional as it authorized the issuance of a writ of immediate possession pending a hearing on the merits in the unlawful detainer action. The named petitioners thereafter abandoned the premises. The superior court then denied the petitions. The court dismissed the petition as to the named petitioners, and granted a peremptory writ to the others. Section 1166a, although it afforded notice and hearing, deprived petitioners of due process because it offended the primary purpose of an unlawful detainer action and flouted the concept of fairness implicit in due process. Section 1166a also deprived insolvent tenants of the equal protection of law upon the basis that the distinction between the solvent and the insolvent in the context of the unlawful detainer statutes has no substantial or reasonable relationship to the legitimate object of an unlawful detainer action.


OUTCOME: The court granted a peremptory writ, in petitioners' landlord-tenant action where the appeals court had denied petitioners' request for a writ of prohibition to preclude the trial court granting the real party in interest immediate possession of the premises in questions in cases where the petitioner tenants were insolvent. The statute section, although affording notice and hearing, deprived insolvent tenants of due process and equal protection.

 

1036 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Adams v. Shannon


Civ. No. 35142


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


7 Cal. App. 3d 427; 86 Cal. Rptr. 641; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 2175



May 8, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, John F. McCarthy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a dealer in tropical fish, sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), denying him an injunction to restrain respondent, the California Department of Fish and Game, from enforcing statutes and regulations prohibiting the importation and possession of piranha.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a tropical fish dealer, imported piranha for sale to the public. Respondent, the Director of the California Department of Fish and Game, served notice upon appellant prohibiting sale of the piranha and requiring him to ship the fish out of state, destroy them, or donate them to a public aquarium. Appellant did not comply with the notice and filed a complaint alleging that the piranha would not pose a threat to natural wildlife if set at large and that Cal. Code Regs. tit. 14.671 was arbitrary and capricious, and seeking an injunction against enforcement of the pertinent regulations and a writ of mandate. The trial court denied appellant's payer for an injunction and writ of mandate and on appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. It held first that appellant's contention that the statutes and regulations prohibiting importation of piranha were unconstitutional was meritless because the determination by the state legislature that the action was necessary to protect the local ecology was a valid exercise of its police power. The court also held that the prohibition was reasonably adapted to its purpose and that appellant had no protected property rights in the fish.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, holding that the statutes and regulations prohibiting the importation and sale of piranha were a valid exercise of the state's police power, were not overbroad or arbitrary and capricious, and did not unconstitutionally deprive appellant of any property rights.

 

1037 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


In re C. D. H.


Civ. No. 27442


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Four


7 Cal. App. 3d 230; 86 Cal. Rptr. 565; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 2155



May 5, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied July 1, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Humboldt County, Donald H. Wilkinson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order is reversed with directions to make new findings and thereupon to take such further proceedings as may be appropriate.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile challenged a judgment from the Superior Court, Humboldt County (California) which adjudged him guilty of violating Cal. Penal Code § 245, assault with a deadly weapon, after he shot one of his companions.


OVERVIEW: Appellant juvenile was charged with assault with a deadly weapon in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 245 after he shot one of his companions in the back with a rifle. On review following his conviction, appellant contended that there was not sufficient evidence to establish that the shooting was other than accidental. The court noted that a recent U.S. Supreme Court holding had made clear that proof beyond a reasonable doubt was the correct standard to apply to juvenile proceedings involving criminal charges. Applying that standard, the court found the evidence sufficient in that appellant had told others just prior to the incident that he intended to shoot and it appeared that appellant loaded the gun. While the evidence suggested that several of the young people present, perhaps including appellant, were intoxicated, the court found that such intoxication would not be a defense where liability was not dependent upon a showing of specific intent. Because the court was unable to determine which standard was used by the lower court to weigh the evidence, it reversed the judgment with directions to the trial court to make findings and enter an appropriate judgment without a new trial.


OUTCOME: Although the reviewing court found sufficient evidence beyond a reasonable doubt that appellant juvenile committed an assault with a deadly weapon, because it could not determine which standard was used by the trial court, it reversed the judgment with directions to the trial court to make findings and enter an appropriate judgment without a new trial.

 

1038 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


In re Donna G.


Crim. No. 17180


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


6 Cal. App. 3d 890; 86 Cal. Rptr. 421; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 1393



April 23, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Robert A. Wenke, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order of commitment appealed from is reversed; the purported appeal from other orders is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner juvenile challenged an order from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) that committed her to the Youth Authority pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 777 after finding that the previous disposition of the juvenile court had not been effective in her rehabilitation.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner juvenile's history included juvenile court findings that she was a dependant child and a ward of the court, but she was retained in her parental home. After she was found in an intoxicated-like condition, the juvenile court issued an order committing her to the Youth Authority pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 777 upon a finding that the previous disposition of that court had not been effective in her rehabilitation. On appeal, the court reversed that commitment order, holding that § 777 was not unconstitutionally vague. The court also held that the facts set forth in the petition and proved at the hearing were not sufficient to meet the statutory standard requiring that the existing program had not been effective in the rehabilitation of the minor. Evidence of a single episode of intoxicated-like behavior did not compel the conclusion that further efforts by petitioner's parents would have been unavailing, and if the juvenile court had considered probation reports in reaching its adjudication, it erred by not summarizing them in the petition and by not proving them at the hearing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order committing petitioner juvenile to the Youth Authority after finding that the previous disposition of the juvenile court had not been effective in her rehabilitation because evidence of a single episode of intoxicated-like behavior did not compel the conclusion that further efforts by petitioner's parents would have been unavailing.

 

1039 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Calzada v. Sinclair


Civ. No. 34500


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


6 Cal. App. 3d 903; 86 Cal. Rptr. 387; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 1395



April 23, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied May 11, 1970, and appellants' petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied June 17, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, A. A. Scott, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, attorney and wife, sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) quieting title to the real property purchased at the trustee's sale in favor of plaintiffs, husband and wife.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, husband and wife, became delinquent in their payments on the note secured by the first deed of trust. They were also in arrears on their payments under the second deed of trust. Defendant wife purchased the second deed of trust, at request of her attorney husband. Defendant attorney was representing plaintiffs in foreclosure matter. At trial for title to the property, the trial court concluded that plaintiffs were not indebted to defendants in any sum and that defendant wife held title to the property in trust for plaintiffs. Plaintiffs were granted title in the real property purchased at the trustee's sale under the second deed of trust. Defendants, attorney and wife, were directed by trial court to execute a quitclaim deed conveying to plaintiffs all right, title and interest of defendants therein. On appeal, the court held that defendant attorney was bound to act in his fiduciary capacity as an attorney at law for the benefit of his clients, but his conduct was tainted with unfairness. Such conduct was sufficient to support the trial court's conclusion that defendant wife held title to the property in trust for plaintiffs. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment quieting title to the real property purchased at the trustee's sale in favor of plaintiffs, husband and wife. Defendant attorney was bound to act in his fiduciary capacity as an attorney at law for the benefit of his clients, but his conduct was tainted with unfairness; this was sufficient to support the trial court's conclusion that defendant wife held title to the property in trust for plaintiffs.

People v. Calder


Crim. No. 16668


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


6 Cal. App. 3d 931; 86 Cal. Rptr. 446; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 1397



April 23, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied June 17, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Edward R. Brand, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), convicting him of being present where narcotics were being smoked or used, a violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11556.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was stopped by a police officer for a traffic violation. Appellant had two tinfoil wrappings in the shape of balls between his belt buckle and belt. The officer asked appellant what the objects were, and appellant answered and handed them to the officer. After the objects were determined to be hashish, appellant was charged with possession of marijuana. Appellant and the prosecutor entered into a stipulation to dismiss the possession charge and to have the trial court find appellant guilty of being present where narcotics were being smoked or used, a less serious offense that possession. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction, holding that because of the stipulation, the fact that the offense for which appellant was convicted was not a lesser-included offense of possession was not relevant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. Appellant was properly convicted for being present where narcotics were being smoked or used, because appellant had entered into a stipulation to be charged with that offense as opposed to the more serious charge of possession of marijuana.

People v. Woods


Crim. No. 16633


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


6 Cal. App. 3d 832; 86 Cal. Rptr. 264; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 1385



April 22, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied May 11, 1970, and respondent's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied June 17, 1970. Sullivan, J., was of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Mario L. Clinco, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order setting aside the information is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The prosecution appealed an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), that granted defendant's motion to set aside an information charging him with possession of marijuana, Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11530, on the ground that police obtained the marijuana by an unconstitutional search and seizure.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested and charged with possession of marijuana under Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11530 after police discovered a bag of marijuana in his pocket. Defendant filed a motion under Cal. Penal Code § 995 to set aside the information on the ground that police obtained the marijuana by an unconstitutional search and seizure. The trial court granted defendant's motion and dismissed the information. The prosecution appealed, contending that the marijuana either was in plain view or was discovered during a reasonable search. The court held that under the circumstances of the case, the police officer had a constitutionally adequate basis to make a nonconsensual stop of defendant, to forcibly withdraw his hand from his pocket to see whether it held a weapon, and to illuminate the interior of that pocket with a flashlight to see why defendant refused to describe what was in his pocket. In reversing the decision granting the motion to set aside the information, the court held that the marijuana in defendant's pocket was not discovered during an unconstitutional search of defendant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court that granted defendant's motion to set aside the information charging him with possession of marijuana because the marijuana evidence against defendant was not discovered by means of an unconstitutional search and seizure.

Rees v. Layton


Civ. Nos. 34935, 34947, 34997


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


6 Cal. App. 3d 815; 86 Cal. Rptr. 268; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 1383



April 21, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied May 8, 1970, and appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied June 17, 1970. Burke, J., was of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Richard Schauer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city clerk sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which issued a writ of mandate compelling appellant to include the respective professions, vocations, or occupations of respondent candidates for office on the ballots for election.


OVERVIEW: Los Angeles County, (California), Elec. Code § 91 allowed only incumbents to have their professions listed on the ballot. Respondent candidates for office challenged § 91 and the trial court granted a writ of mandate compelling appellant city clerk to include respondents' professions on the ballots. The court affirmed the order issuing the writ of mandate, holding that § 91 imposed an invidious requirement, which violated the equal protection clauses of both U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Cal. Const. art. XI § 81/2. The court found that § 91 provided an unfair advantage to incumbents over non-incumbents and that there was no rational basis for the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting a writ of mandate, holding that the city election code, which allowed only the incumbents to have their occupation listed on the ballot, was an invidious requirement, violative of the equal protection clause.

Montgomery Ward & Co. v. Franchise Tax Bd.


Civ. No. 26105


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


6 Cal. App. 3d 149; 85 Cal. Rptr. 890; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 1317



March 31, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied May 28, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, Melvyn I. Cronin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed with respect to those issues resolved by the lower court, it is nevertheless set aside and the case is remanded solely for determination of the amount due the taxpayer pursuant to the provisions of paragraph 22, of the stipulation of facts, and for correction of the judgment accordingly. Let respondent recover its costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) which denied it recovery of a portion of its corporate franchise taxes assessed and paid for six income years. Plaintiff contended that defendant Franchise Tax Board erred in allocating its income because it included property in transit to California in the numerator of the property factor used in the income allocation formula.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff taxpayer, a corporation that operated a nationwide retail business, was taxed based upon income that was a portion of its total net income which the taxing authorities found to be derived from, or attributable to, sources within California. Plaintiff filed suit against defendant Franchise Tax Board, seeking recovery of a portion of its corporate franchise taxes assessed and paid for six income years. The trial court denied plaintiff's claim. On appeal, plaintiff contended that defendant erred in allocating its income because it included property in transit to California in the numerator of the property factor used in the income allocation formula. The court affirmed the judgment with respect to the issues resolved by the trial court, but remanded for a determination of the amount due to plaintiff pursuant to a stipulation between the parties. The court reasoned that defendant only included in the measure that property which was unconditionally appropriated for utilization in California, and which, was neither taxed elsewhere, nor used as a measure of income derived from or attributable to another taxing jurisdiction. Thus, the formula was not erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment with respect to the issues resolved by the trial court, but remanded for a determination of the amount due to plaintiff taxpayer pursuant to a stipulation between the parties. The court ruled that the formula used by defendant Franchise Tax Board to calculate the tax was proper because it reflected the portion of plaintiff's total property that was appropriated for the production of income in California.

 

1045 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hurd


Crim. Nos. 3639, 3640


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


5 Cal. App. 3d 865; 85 Cal. Rptr. 718; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 1485



March 24, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Orange County, Raymond Thompson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Superior Court of Orange County (California) on four counts of incest, three counts of oral copulation, and one count of sodomy, stemming from sexual activity engaged in between him and his 16-year old daughter.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted on four counts of incest, three counts of oral copulation, and one count of sodomy, stemming from sexual activity engaged in between him and his 16-year old daughter. On appeal, defendant argued that the statutes proscribing incest, sodomy, and oral copulation, as applied to the facts of his case, constituted unconstitutional infringements by the state of his right of privacy. The court disagreed and affirmed. The court held that defendant could not cite any authority that the right of privacy constitutionally protected under the penumbra doctrine extended to a father's sexual contact with his minor daughter. The court further held that the penal statutes proscribing illicit sexual contact constituted a proper exercise of the state's police power. Further, evidence of uncharged sex offenses were admissible where they were committed on the victim of the charged offense, were in a nature similar to the charged offense, were committed at a point in time to the charged offense, and evidence of the charged offenses were substantially corroborated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction on four counts of incest, three counts of oral copulation, and one count of sodomy, stemming from sexual activity between him and his 16-year old daughter. The court held that in the exercise of its police powers, the state had the right to enact laws to promote public health, safety, morals, and welfare; penal statutes proscribing illicit sexual contact constituted a proper exercise of that power.

 

1046 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Gee v. California State Personnel Board


Civ. No. 26331


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


5 Cal. App. 3d 713; 85 Cal. Rptr. 762; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 1474



March 20, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied May 15, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, Robert J. Drewes, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) denying his petition for a writ of mandamus, for review of a decision of defendant personnel board, which dismissed petitioner from his civil servant position for dishonesty, as set forth in Cal. Gov't Code § 19572. Plaintiff argued that the law did not authorize dismissal for acts that occurred prior to his employment.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff employee was dismissed from his civil service position based on false statements made by plaintiff in applications for three on-sale liquor licenses. It was later discovered that plaintiff was not the owner of any of the businesses, but merely received a percentage of the profits for supplying the licenses. After defendant personnel board sustained the dismissal, plaintiff filed a petition for a writ of mandamus, which the trial court denied. On appeal, plaintiff argued that defendant's findings were not supported by substantial evidence and that the law did not authorize dismissal for acts that occurred prior to his employment. The appeals court affirmed. The court ruled that defendant's finding that plaintiff knew that his arrangement violated the Alcoholic Beverage Control Act was amply supported by the unusual and clandestine nature of the operation and his statement under oath that no person other than himself would have any direct or indirect interest in the businesses. The court also ruled that plaintiff's removal for dishonesty was proper, since his duties called for him to investigate the same type of business offense that he committed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed plaintiff's dismissal from his civil service position for dishonesty occurring prior to his employment. The court ruled that because plaintiff was found to have shown serious attributes of dishonesty, unknown to the state prior to his employment, he was properly dismissed when the dishonesty was discovered, since his position called for him to investigate similar offenses.

Bailey v. Superior Court of Ventura County


Civ. No. 35503


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


4 Cal. App. 3d 513; 84 Cal. Rptr. 436; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 1553



February 18, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitioner's application for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied April 15, 1970. Peters, J., and Sullivan, J., were of the opinion that the petition should be granted.



DISPOSITION: The alternative writ of prohibition heretofore issued is discharged. The petition for a peremptory writ of prohibition is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Ventura County (California), which denied defendants motion for demurrer and motion to set aside the information in defendants trial for violation of Cal. Veh. Code § 20001.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with violating Cal. Veh. Code § 20001 after defendant failed to identify himself at the scene of an auto accident in which he was involved and failed to render aid to the injured parties in the other car. The court found that defendant could not be charged under the provision of § 20001 which required defendant to identify himself because such compelled disclosure violated defendant's U.S. Const. amend. V privilege against self-incrimination. However, the court denied defendant's petition for writ of prohibition and found that the portion of § 20001 that required defendant to render aid did not violate his privilege against self-incrimination because the privilege only applied to evidence of communications or testimony of defendant and not to real or physical evidence derived from him.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's writ of prohibition because state law that required a person involved in an auto accident to render assistance to injured parties did not violate defendant's privilege against self-incrimination.

 

1048 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Stoddard v. Edelman


Civ. No. 33790


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


4 Cal. App. 3d 544; 84 Cal. Rptr. 443; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 1557



February 18, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied April 15, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Robert S. Thompson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners property owners sought review of an order denying a mandate by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which affirmed approval by respondent city council of a conditional use permit for a church to respondents developer and congregation, which had been denied by respondent city's zoning administrator. Petitioners claimed the Los Angeles Municipal Code was unconstitutionally vague and the permit was not authorized.


OVERVIEW: Respondents developer and congregation were denied a conditional use permit to build a church by respondent city's zoning administrator, which denial was affirmed by respondent city's board of zoning adjustments. Respondent city council granted the permit and petitioners property owners sought a mandate in the trial court to set aside the decision to grant the permit, which the trial court denied. Petitioners sought reversal of the trial court's denial and claimed that the Los Angeles Municipal Code under which the permit was granted was unconstitutionally vague, violated due process, and the permit was outside the scope of Cal. Gov't Code § 65901. The court affirmed the trial court's order and held that § 65901 authorized respondent city to issue the permit, since respondent city had established criteria and procedures for permit requests, pursuant to Los Angeles, Cal., Municipal Code § 12.02, which were sufficiently specific to satisfy due process and had been followed by respondents. The court further held that conditional use permits, which did not rezone, did not have to comply with respondent city's rezoning procedures.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of petitioners property owners' request for a mandate, because respondents city and developer had complied with the permit ordinance scheme, which was not unconstitutionally vague.

 

1049 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Dorow v. Santa Clara County Flood Control Dist.


Civ. No. 25742


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


4 Cal. App. 3d 389; 84 Cal. Rptr. 518; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 1538



February 16, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Santa Clara County, Bruce F. Allen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Without prejudice to such rights, asserted in any appropriate proceeding, the summary judgment herein is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), which granted summary judgment for respondent flood control district. Appellant sought to recover damages under Cal. Const. art. I, § 14, for an alleged taking and damaging of her private property for public use. Appellant did not file a claim for inverse condemnation prior to filing suit, as required by Cal. Gov't. Code §§ 905, 911.2, 945.4.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of respondent flood control district in appellant landowner's action for inverse condemnation. The county acquired an easement for creek bed improvements in 1878 and filed a lis pendens, but the decree in condemnation was not recorded until 1959, when the county quitclaimed its interest to respondent by recorded deed. Appellant purchased the property through which the creek flowed in 1953. Respondent completed the installation of a box culvert or pipes in appellant's portion of the creek bed, which it filled over with dirt, in 1963. The court held that appellant had no cause of action against respondent because respondent utilized the easement. The court held that appellant's action was also barred because she did not file a timely claim for compensation as required by Cal. Gov't. Code §§ 905, 911.2, 945.4 after she knew of the improvement by respondent. Compliance with the claims requirements was a condition precedent to a suit for damages for inverse condemnation under Cal. Const. art. I, § 14. Finally, the court held that the claims requirement as applied to inverse condemnation was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of respondent flood control district in appellant landowner's inverse condemnation action. Respondent used the easement for creek bed improvements. Appellant did not file a timely claim for compensation prior to bringing the inverse condemnation proceeding. The claims statute requirement as applied to inverse condemnation was constitutional.

 

1050 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Livingston


Crim. No. 7493


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


4 Cal. App. 3d 251; 84 Cal. Rptr. 237; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 1523



February 9, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, Harry J. Neubarth, Judge.



DISPOSITION: We find no error and the judgment of conviction is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which convicted defendant for violation of Cal. Penal Code § 12021, a felon in possession of a concealed weapon, and for violation of Cal. Penal Code § 245, assault with a deadly weapon on a police officer.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for violation of Cal. Penal Code § 12021, a felon in possession of a concealed weapon, and for violation of Cal. Penal Code § 245, assault with a deadly weapon. Defendant was stopped by police as a suspect for looking into parked automobiles. During questioning, defendant pulled out a revolver and pointed it at the officer. The court affirmed defendant's convictions and concluded that defendant was a felon within the meaning of § 1202, and the fact that he served time in a county jail did not mean he was convicted of a misdemeanor. His confinement in county jail was imposed as a condition of probation after conviction of a felony. Defendant also failed to demonstrate ineffective assistance of counsel or that the trial was reduced to a sham. Defendant accused his attorney of being derelict in failing to locate an alibi witness, but the record showed that defendant gave the name of the witness to his counsel the day before the trial. The court finally found that the intent to commit the assault could be inferred from the wrongful act, and held that defendant's initial detention was lawful since the police had a duty to investigate all suspicious activities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for possession of a concealed weapon as a felon and for assault with a deadly weapon on a police officer. The court concluded that defendant was a felon within the meaning of the statute and that he had failed to demonstrate the ineffectiveness of counsel. The court held that the specific intent to commit the assault on the police officer could be inferred from the wrongful act.

 

1051 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Golden Gate Bridge & Highway Dist. v. Luehring


Civ. No. 26995


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Four


4 Cal. App. 3d 204; 84 Cal. Rptr. 291; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 1518



February 6, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The alternative writ is discharged and the petition is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners highway district and directors sought mandate to compel respondent district general manager and auditor to issue warrants for payment of certain surplus revenues of the district to the county governments of the counties comprised within the district.


OVERVIEW: The court discharged the writ and denied petitioners highway district and directors request to compel respondent district general manager and auditor to issue warrants for payment of certain surplus revenues of the district to the county governments of the counties comprised within the district. The court concluded that the purpose of petitioners was bridging the Golden Gate to provide access between counties for those wishing to cross, and not drumming up as many persons as possible to make the crossing. The court found that the only apparent way in which additional users would promote the interests of petitioners would be by furnishing additional revenue, necessary for adequate maintenance of, or addition to, the facilities provided for bridging the Golden Gate. The court concluded there was no showing that petitioners were languishing because of inadequate traffic on the bridge, and that there was no showing that the transfer of these monies to the counties would promote the interests of the district in any substantial way. The court concluded that the proposed transfers would not advance the district's purposes even though the counties could use the money.


OUTCOME: The alternative writ was discharged and the petition was denied, and the court concluded that the proposed payments, although purportedly authorized by statute, were contrary to the constitution, and that there was no showing petitioners highway district and directors were languishing because of inadequate traffic on the bridge.

 

1052 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


W. & S. Life Ins. Co. v. State Bd. of Equalization


Civ. No. 33497


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


4 Cal. App. 3d 21; 84 Cal. Rptr. 88; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 1500



January 30, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied February 10, 1970, and the petitions of the appellant and the respondent for a hearing by the Supreme Court were denied April 22, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Brodie Ahlport, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed with directions to the trial court to enter judgment in favor of the plaintiff and against the defendant in the sum of $ 120,303.93 with interest thereon in accordance with the provisions of section 13107 of the Revenue and Taxation Code.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff challenged the order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) holding that the retaliatory tax provision of Cal. Const. art. XIII, § 14-4/5, was properly assessed by defendant against plaintiff's tax liability for 1964.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sought the recovery of a refund of a sum paid as the result of a retaliatory tax levied against it under Cal. Const. art. XIII, § 14-4/5. Plaintiff was an out-of-state corporation licensed to do business in California. In 1964, the retaliatory tax provision was amended. In computing plaintiff's taxes, defendant applied the retaliatory tax, as amended, against its assessment of plaintiff's tax liability for 1964. On appeal, plaintiff contended that the retaliatory tax as amended was only applicable to foreign insurers who were admitted after the amendment. The court held that a state can prescribe the terms and conditions on which business is conducted within its borders and that such retaliatory taxes must be strictly construed. Since nothing in the legislative history indicated an intent to apply the 1964 amendment retrospectively, it could only be applied prospectively.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, because, strictly construed, the amended retaliatory tax provision was not to be applied retrospectively against plaintiff's tax liability for 1964.

People v. Koch


Crim. No. 15376


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


4 Cal. App. 3d 270; 84 Cal. Rptr. 629; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 1526



January 29, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied March 25, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Richard F. C. Hayden, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment as to count 2 (grand theft) is reversed. The judgment as to count 1 (conspiracy) is reversed with directions to the trial court: (1) to strike the finding that defendant was found guilty of conspiracy to commit grand theft and to enter in its place the finding that he was found guilty of conspiracy in violation of Penal Code, section 182, subdivision 4; (2) to thereafter conduct another hearing on probation and sentence. In all other respects the judgment as to count 1 is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted defendant in a nonjury trial of conspiracy to commit grand theft under Cal. Penal Code § 182 and grand theft under Cal. Penal Code § 487(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of conspiracy to commit grand theft under Cal. Penal Code § 182 and grand theft under Cal. Penal Code § 487(1). The record showed that defendant obtained unemployment benefits after making false claims based on non-existing former employment and used fictitious names. The evidence supported the inference that the benefits were secured in pursuance of a scheme concocted by defendant and another party. The court concluded that defendant's conviction for grand theft must be reversed because defendant should not have been prosecuted under § 487(1), but rather for the misdemeanor offense under Cal. Unemp. Ins. Code § 2101. The court concluded that the judgment of the lower court with respect to conspiracy was to be modified to adjudge that defendant was found guilty of the crime of conspiracy in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 182(4), rather than of the crime of conspiracy to commit grand theft in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 182(1). Defendant was also entitled to another probation and sentencing hearing on the conspiracy conviction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment as to the grand theft count because defendant was charged under the inappropriate penal statute. The court reversed the trial court's judgment as to the conspiracy count with directions to the trial court to strike the finding that defendant was found guilty of conspiracy to commit grand theft and to enter the finding that he was found guilty of conspiracy in violation of a penal statute.

 

1054 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Chico Unified School Dist. v. Board of Supervisors


Civ. No. 11988


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


3 Cal. App. 3d 852; 84 Cal. Rptr. 198; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 1177



January 23, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Butte County, J. F. Good, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county board of supervisors sought review of a writ of mandate issued by the Superior Court of Butte County (California), which determined that appellant was obligated to pay respondent school district a proportionate share of monies repaid to the state for building facilities for exceptional children.


OVERVIEW: Respondent school district requested appellant county board of supervisors to pay its pro rata share, as required by Cal. Educ. Code § 19685, of the cost of construction for a facility used for programs for exceptional children. Appellant refused to pay on the basis that it had no knowledge of the construction and had made no appropriation for the facility in the budget. The lower court issued a writ of mandate that directed appellant to pay the monies owed to respondent. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that § 19685 did not violate Cal. Const. art. XI, § 13, because it did not delegate to any individual any power to levy taxes or assessments. The court concluded that the school district was an agency of the state and that § 19685 provided for tuition assessments as well as tax assessments for paying the cost of construction. The court held that § 19685 required appellant to reimburse respondent its pro rata share of the construction costs, even though not in the budget, because § 19685 was mandatory in requiring appellant to reimburse respondent even if the request was made after appellant's budget was approved.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the issuance of a writ of mandate that required appellant county board of supervisors to pay respondent school district its pro rata share for the construction of facilities for exceptional children because the statutory language requiring reimbursement was mandatory and the statute at issue was not unconstitutional.

 

1055 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Connelly v. State


Civ. No. 1057


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


3 Cal. App. 3d 744; 84 Cal. Rptr. 257; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 1168



January 21, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The petitions of the appellant and the respondents for a hearing by the Supreme Court were denied April 1, 1970. Burke, J., was of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sacramento County, Irving H. Perluss, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed insofar as the first and fourth causes of action are concerned, and the case is remanded to the trial court with instructions to permit appellant to amend his first and fourth causes of action if he is so disposed. The judgment is affirmed as to the second, third and fifth causes of action.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant marina owner sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which sustained respondents', state and state agency, demurrer without leave to amend in appellant's action to recover for flood damages.


OVERVIEW: Appellant marina owner called respondent state agency to inquire about changes in the level of a swollen river. Appellant relied on the information and suffered damage when the river rose beyond respondent state agency's expectations. The trial court granted respondents', state and state agency, demurrer. On appeal, the court found that respondents' demurrer was properly sustained as to the causes which were unsupported by a precedent claim as required by Cal. Gov't Code § 910 et seq. However, the court found that appellant could amend his complaint to allege sufficient facts to state a negligence claim and, thus, respondents' demurrer should not have been sustained as to alleged negligence in the dissemination of inaccurate river height forecasts. The court held that the determination to issue flood forecasts was a policy-making function, which was a discretionary activity within the scope of governmental immunity. However, the gathering, evaluating, and dissemination of flood forecast information was administrative and outside the scope of immunity. Because there was nothing in the pleadings about policy or decision making, the demurrer as to those causes of action was reversed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the judgment that sustained respondents', state and state agency, demurrer in appellant marina owner's action for flood damages and held that respondents' demurrer should not have been sustained as to appellant's claims that were predicated on alleged negligence in the dissemination of inaccurate river height forecasts. The remaining claims were unsupported by a precedent negligence claim.

Hoffman v. Municipal Court for Oakland-Piedmont Judicial Dist.


Civ. No. 26302


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


3 Cal. App. 3d 621; 83 Cal. Rptr. 747; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 1158



January 20, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied April 1, 1970. Peters, J., and Tobriner, J., were of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Alameda County, Folger Emerson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney challenged an order of the Superior Court of Alameda County (California), which denied his petition for a writ of prohibition. Appellant was charged with violating Cal. Penal Code §§ 415, 409, and 647c, and contended these sections were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant attorney was charged with violations of Cal. Penal Code § 415 for unlawful, willful and malicious disturbing of the peace by "tumultuous and offensive conduct," Cal. Penal Code § 409 because he remained present at the place of a riot, rout and unlawful assembly, and Cal. Penal Code § 647c for unlawful, willful and malicious obstruction of the free movement of persons on a place open to the public. Appellant contended the statutes were unconstitutional and petitioned for a writ of prohibition, which was denied. On appeal, the court affirmed the order denying the writ and held that § 415 and § 409 were not unconstitutional for vagueness or overbreadth. The court concluded that appellant was not a "public official" within the meaning of § 409 and, therefore, it was applicable to him. The court held that the complaint, which used the language of the statutes, apprised appellant of the conduct giving rise to the charges. Finally, the court held that § 647c was constitutionally applicable to appellant, who claimed to have been in the act of giving advice to his client, and that whether or not appellant could be convicted was a question of fact to be determined at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order and held that none of the statutes were vague or overbroad, that the complaint apprised appellant attorney of the conduct which gave rise to the charges, and that the statute applied to appellant because he was not a "public officer" within the meaning of the statute.

American President Lines, Ltd. v. Franchise Tax Board


Civ. No. 26262


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


3 Cal. App. 3d 587; 83 Cal. Rptr. 702; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 1154



January 19, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, Raymond J. Arata, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of an order of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which entered a judgment in favor of respondent Franchise Tax Board (board) in appellant's action for a refund of franchise taxes it paid to the board under protest pursuant to Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 23151.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayer challenged the trial court's judgment in favor of respondent Franchise Tax Board (board). Appellant, in seeking a refund of franchise taxes, contended that it engaged only in interstate commerce and was not subject to the state franchise tax, and that even if it were, the board erred in allocating to California all of appellant's federal reserve fund interest. The board and trial court agreed that appellant's services as a steamship corporation engaged as both a husbanding and general agent for the transportation of passengers and property between American and foreign ports, were intrastate activities subject to corporation franchise tax under Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 23151; that the reserve fund interest was includable in appellant's taxable income, and; that the interest was wholly allocable to California as appellant's commercial domicile. The court affirmed, holding that appellant's local business activities were separate from its own interstate and foreign commerce activities, and that all of appellant's reserve fund interest income was allocable to California because it was not part of the unitary business's operating income and not subject to apportionment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of respondent Franchise Tax Board (board) in appellant taxpayer's action for a refund of franchise taxes, because appellant's transportation services and general agent activities were intrastate activities separate from appellant's own interstate activities and thus were subject to franchise tax, and the board properly allocated appellant's reserve fund interest income to California.

 

1058 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Superior Court of Santa Clara County


Civ. Nos. 27414, 27418, Crim. No. 8278


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


3 Cal. App. 3d 476; 83 Cal. Rptr. 771; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 1141



January 14, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Let the peremptory writ of mandate issue in 1 Civil 27414 commanding respondeat superior court to annul and set aside its order granting the motion to suppress evidence and to enter a new order denying defendant's motion to suppress the evidence pursuant to section 1538.5. The peremptory writ of prohibition is denied and the alternative writ of prohibition is discharged in 1 Civil 27418. The order to show cause is discharged and the petition for a writ of habeas corpus is denied in 1 Criminal 8278.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought a writ of habeas corpus against the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California) through Cal. Penal Code § 1538.5(k) after his motion to suppress evidence was granted. The state sought a writ of mandate for review of the order which suppressed evidence and sought a writ of prohibition to stay the trial pending adjudication of the merits of the petition for writ of mandate.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought a writ of habeas corpus against the superior court through Cal. Penal Code § 1538.5(k) after his motion to suppress evidence was granted. The state sought a writ of mandate for review of the order which suppressed evidence. The court held that defendant's statement "Over on the kitchen sink" contributed to the discovery of the murder weapon, a knife, but that the knife would have been discovered by the police because it was in plain sight even if the subject statement had not been made. The court held that securing of the knife was purged of any primary taint that might have attached to it on the basis that the statement was illegally obtained. The court held that Cal. Penal Code § 1538.5 was proper for bringing a motion to suppress evidence on the ground that it was obtained as the fruit of an illegal statement, and that when the motion to suppress was granted, the state was entitled to petition for a writ of mandate as provided by § 1538.5(o) to review the validity of the order. The court granted the writ of mandate and commanded the superior court to annul and set aside its order which granted the motion to suppress evidence.


OUTCOME: The court issued the writ of mandate requested by the state because the evidence was admissible and the order which suppressed the evidence was required to be annulled, and the proceedings were to be resumed. Defendant's motion for habeas corpus was deemed to be moot since defendant would have had to have been returned to custody upon resumption of the proceedings.

Feist v. Rowe


Civ. No. 9328


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


3 Cal. App. 3d 404; 83 Cal. Rptr. 465; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 1136



January 9, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied January 23, 1970, and the petition of plaintiff and appellant for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied March 4, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, Robert O. Staniforth, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment that a writ of mandate issue is reversed and the trial court directed to enter judgment in favor of Rowe and Board on the first cause of action of petitioner's complaint.

Rowe and Board shall recover costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, school board and superintendent, sought review of an order of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which granted a writ of mandamus in favor of petitioner teacher, that commanded either a rehearing in the dismissal proceedings against petitioner as a probationary teacher or, in the alternative, reinstatement as a regular, full-time, certificated teacher.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Cal. Educ. Code § 13443, petitioner teacher, a probationary teacher, was given notice by respondents, school board and superintendent, that her services would not be required for the ensuing school year. The trial court granted a writ of mandamus in favor of petitioner, which commanded either a rehearing or reinstatement as a regular teacher. On appeal, the court reversed and held that the evidence was sufficient and the decision of respondent school board should have been sustained. The hearing officer did not allow petitioner to present evidence of discrimination, but that was within his discretion. There was no deprivation of fair hearing and due process because Cal. Gov't Code § 11512 permitted a delegation by respondent board of all its functions of fact-finder and decision-maker even after its earlier intention to exercise such functions directly. It was the burden of petitioner to show error by respondent board. The complete transcript was not available for examination to determine what was offered during the course of the hearing or to determine if there was prejudice. The limited transcript did not show evidence that the hearing officer was in error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that a writ of mandate should issue and held that petitioner teacher had not sustained her burden to show error by respondent school board. The court directed the trial court to enter judgment in favor of respondents, school board and superintendent, and awarded respondents costs on appeal.

People v. Kraft


Crim. No. 5344


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


3 Cal. App. 3d 890; 84 Cal. Rptr. 280; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 1184



January 9, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
A petition for a rehearing was denied February 6, 1970. David, J. pro tem., * was of the opinion that the petition should be granted. Respondent's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied March 4, 1970. McComb, J., was of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


* Retired judge of the superior court sitting under assignment by the Chairman of the Judicial Council.


PRIOR HISTORY: Municipal Court of the Sacramento Judicial District of Sacramento County, John J. Boskovich, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of misdemeanor drunk driving pursuant to Cal. Veh. Code § 23102(a) in municipal court. Defendant sought review of the municipal court's decision in the appellate division of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which affirmed the municipal court's conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was observed by police officers driving on the wrong side of the road and was arrested after he failed roadside tests. Subsequently, defendant steadfastly refused blood tests at the hospital. A blood test was taken after a police officer struck defendant with a closed fist. Defendant's blood alcohol level was entered into evidence, and defendant was convicted of misdemeanor drunk driving pursuant to Cal. Veh. Code § 23102(a) in municipal court. Defendant sought review in the appellate division of the superior court, which affirmed his conviction. The court accepted certification under Cal. R. Ct. 63(a) to secure uniformity and settle questions of law. The court reversed the conviction of misdemeanor drunk driving. The court held that the U.S. Const. amend. IV's bounds of reasonableness were exceeded because defendant's blood test was not drawn according to accepted medical practices. The court reasoned that, although the factual determination of excessive force would normally be entitled to great weight, the municipal judge improperly focused on the technical, rather than forceful, aspects of defendant's blood test.


OUTCOME: The court accepted certification and reversed the decision of the lower court that affirmed defendant's conviction. The court determined that because the police used unlawfully excessive force to obtain the blood alcohol test, accepted medical practices were not followed and the constitutional bounds of reasonableness were exceeded. Therefore, the judgment of conviction required reversal.

Greyhound Lines, Inc. v. Superior Court of Shasta County


Civ. No. 12303


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


3 Cal. App. 3d 356; 83 Cal. Rptr. 343; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 1133



January 8, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitioner's application for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied March 4, 1970. McComb, J., was of the opinion that the petition should be granted.



DISPOSITION: The writ is denied. The order to show cause is discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner common carrier challenged, through writ of prohibition, the decision of respondent, the Superior Court of Shasta County (California), which overruled petitioner's demurrers and denied it motion for summary judgment, in the negligent failure to provide seat belt actions of real party in interest passengers.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner bus line was transporting real party in interest passengers from San Francisco to Vancouver, when the bus collided with a truck in the county of respondent court. Real parties brought negligence actions, some of which alleged that petitioner was negligent in failing to equip its bus with passenger seat belts. Petitioner demurred to the seat belt causes of action, contending that respondent lacked jurisdiction over them due to federal preemption. The trial court overruled the demurrer and a subsequent motion for summary judgment. Petitioner sought a writ of prohibition. On review the court denied the writ, holding that as there was no controlling federal law or regulation, it concluded that under California decisional law it was for the jury to decide whether the carrier's failure to provide seat belts amounted to negligence. The court noted that the toll of highway injury and death was such that judicial policy should be against deferment to legislative inaction and in favor of having juries pass upon the question until such time as the legislature chose to adopt supervising safety regulations.


OUTCOME: The court denied the writ because, as there was no controlling federal law or regulation, under California decisional law it was for the jury to decide whether the petitioner common carrier's failure to provide seat belts amounted to negligence.

 

1062 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Seastone


Crim. No. 728


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


3 Cal. App. 3d 60; 82 Cal. Rptr. 907; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1361



December 29, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Sacramento County, Albert H. Mundt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California) for first-degree murder in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 187. Defendant contended that the superior court erred in admitting certain photographic evidence at trial, that the superior court failed to properly instruct the jurors regarding unanimity, and that it was error to deny his motion to reduce the crime to second-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for the first-degree murder of his infant son and was sentenced to life imprisonment. Defendant contended that the superior court erred in admitting certain photographic evidence at trial, that it failed to properly instruct the jurors, and that it was error to deny his motion to reduce the crime to second-degree murder. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and concluded that the superior court did not abuse its discretion in admitting photographs into evidence showing the bruised condition of most of the infant's body. The court found that the primary purpose of the photographs was not to inflame the jury against defendant but were primarily relevant in that they revealed injures so brutally inflicted as to show an abandoned and malignant heart and supported the prosecution's theory of sexual motivation for the crime. The court held that the superior court was not required to instruct the jurors that they had to agree unanimously on the theory upon which they determined guilt. Finally, the court found no error in the rejection of medical opinion regarding defendant's diminished capacity and in the denial of a motion to reduce the degree of the crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment of conviction against defendant for first-degree murder and concluded that the evidence supported the verdict of first-degree murder under any of the prosecution's three theories. The court found no error in the rejection of medical opinion regarding diminished capacity and in the superior court's denial of the motion to reduce the degree of the crime.

People v. Taylor


Crim. No. 7217


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


2 Cal. App. 3d 979; 83 Cal. Rptr. 119; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1481



December 23, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied January 14, 1970, and appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied February 18, 1970. Peters, J., was of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Alameda County, Redmond C. Staats, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The superior court will modify its judgment and commitment to indicate that the only prior felony conviction admitted or proved was defendant Taylor's conviction of burglary in the Alameda County Superior Court on or about September 20, 1962; as so modified the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Alameda County (California), which convicted defendant of receiving stolen property, a violation of Cal. Penal Code § 496 and possession of a concealable firearm by one previously convicted of a felony, a violation of Cal. Penal Code § 12021. Defendant acted as his own attorney at the trial.


OVERVIEW: A police officer was driving in an area where many burglaries had occurred when he saw a man dart across the street and disappear. The policeman pursued while calling for assistance. However, visual contact was lost. Ten minutes later, the policeman saw one of the responding officers apprehend defendant. Checking over the police radio, officers learned that defendant was on parole and that he had been arrested for burglaries and other offenses in the past. They also learned that a burglary had been committed shortly before. Defendant was placed under arrest and his vehicle was searched. The police found ammunition, both expended and unexpended. Later, a stolen revolver was found near where defendant was apprehended. It was determined that the shells in defendant's car had been fired from the revolver. The court rejected defendant's contention that the search of his automobile at the time of his arrest was violative of Fourth and Fourteenth Amendment standards. The court held that having reasonable cause to believe that defendant committed a burglary, it was reasonable for police to conclude that the vehicle, which was immediately before them, might contain stolen property.


OUTCOME: The court modified it judgment and commitment to indicate that the only prior felony conviction admitted or proved was defendant's conviction of burglary. The court affirmed the judgment as modified.

 

1064 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lundy


Crim. No. 15795


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


2 Cal. App. 3d 939; 82 Cal. Rptr. 815; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1477



December 22, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied February 18, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Thomas F. McCarry, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The appeal from the order of July 3, 1968, denying defendant's propria persona motion for a new trial and to vacate the judgment is dismissed; the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted him of two counts of first degree robbery. Defendant also appealed an order of the trial court, which denied defendant's motion for a new trial and to vacate the judgment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree robbery. He filed a motion for a new trial, which the trial court denied, and then appealed from the judgment. After notice of appeal from the judgment had been filed, defendant filed a motion for a new trial and a motion to vacate the judgment. Those motions were denied. Defendant filed an appeal from that order. The court dismissed that appeal. The court held that the attempt to move for a new trial, being made after judgment, was not timely; being made after the appeal had been taken, the trial had no jurisdiction, and even if timely and within the trial court's jurisdiction, the order was not appealable. The court affirmed the conviction. The court held that its examination of a photograph of defendant disclosed nothing that would justify overriding the trial court's finding that the lineup was not unconstitutionally unfair. The court held further that the trial court's giving of Cal. Jury Instructions Crim. No. 51 (Re-revised), on the failure of defendant to testify, was not error. The court held also that there was no illegality in regard to a search of a car and that admission of certain evidence was not prejudicial to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and dismissed defendant's appeal from the trial court's order denying his motions for a new trial and to vacate the judgment.
