Williams v. Department of Motor Vehicles


Civ. No. 33380


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


2 Cal. App. 3d 949; 83 Cal. Rptr. 76; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1478



December 22, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Robert S. Thompson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment ordering the issuance of the writ is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Department of Motor Vehicles (department) sought review of the order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted respondent driver's petition for writ of mandate. The driver had been convicted of driving while under the influence of intoxicating liquor. The trial court recommended no suspension of the driver's operator's license.


OVERVIEW: The driver was convicted by a municipal court of another violation of driving while under the influence of intoxicating liquor. The department suspended the driver's license for one year and ordered the driver to surrender his license to the department. The driver filed a petition for writ of mandate to set aside and revoke its order of suspension of his license to operate a motor vehicle, which was granted. The department contended on appeal that it acted under a mandatory duty by suspending the driver's license and that the suspension was not penal in nature. The department also asserted that the driver could not collaterally attack his judgment of conviction. The court affirmed the issuance of the writ of mandate by the trial court on the basis that the trial court did have the authority not to suspend the driver's license. However, the court reversed the writ of mandate because it found that as long as the driver's first conviction remained in effect, the department was under no duty to return the driver's license during the period of suspension provided by law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the issuance of the writ of mandate to the driver in the department's appeal of the trial court's grant of the writ to the driver.

 

1066 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Diamond


Crim. No. 681


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


2 Cal. App. 3d 860; 83 Cal. Rptr. 11; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1470



December 18, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied January 15, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Fresno County, Leonard I. Meyers, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgments are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of their respective convictions in the Superior Court of Fresno County (California) for possession of a combustible substance, in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 452(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendants, all young African-Americans, were arrested five days after the assassination of Dr. Martin Luther King and charged with possession of a combustible substance, in violation of § 452(a). There had been some disturbances in the city over the assassination and the police had received reports that African-Americans had threatened to burn the mall. Defendants' car was observed traveling in the area of the mall and the vehicle was allegedly maneuvered in an attempt to avoid passing a police car. A police officer stopped defendant's car. In plain view on the floor of the car, the officer saw, inter alia, certain bottles, wooden clubs, matches, and a rolled paper having a gasoline odor. The bottles contained a mixture of gas and oil. Defendants were convicted. On appeal, the court rejected defendants' claims that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and that the evidence was insufficient to support the convictions. The court also rejected defendants' contention that the officer had no justification to stop their car, finding that the officer had cause to stop defendants' vehicle to conduct a reasonable investigation. Thus, the seizure of the contraband was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions for possession of a combustible substance.

 

1067 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Nelson


Crim. No. 16343


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


2 Cal. App. 3d 738; 83 Cal. Rptr. 6; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1462



December 17, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Malcolm M. Lucas, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment (order granting probation) is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted him of unauthorized alteration of identification number on a handgun and of carrying a loaded firearm without a permit in a public place, and which granted probation.


OVERVIEW: Police officers were alerted to four suspicious men in an alley. The officers went to the alley, and one of them saw defendant crouch down to hide. Defendant was ordered to come out, and when he did, the officers conducted a cursory search for weapons. A loaded pistol was found on defendant. One of the officers then turned his flashlight on the spot where defendant had been crouching and observed a revolver located about three inches from where defendant's right leg had been. The revolver was found to be loaded and the official serial number on the butt end of the revolver had been removed, but the serial number had not been removed from two secret locations where the manufacturer had placed the number. Defendant was convicted of unauthorized alteration of identification number on a handgun and of carrying a loaded firearm without a permit in a public place. The court held that the crime of unauthorized alteration of identification number on a handgun was complete upon the removal of the identification number from the frame of the revolver. The court determined that the fact that other serial numbers on the revolver had not been altered was immaterial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

People v. Rojas


Crim. No. 742


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


2 Cal. App. 3d 767; 82 Cal. Rptr. 862; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1464



December 17, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Yolo County, James C. McDermott, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order from the Superior Court of Yolo County (California), which adjudicated him a narcotic addict and ordered his commitment to the department of corrections with ultimate confinement in a narcotic rehabilitation facility. Defendant had pled guilty to unlawfully selling and furnishing heroin and to having a prior conviction of a felony offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged by an indictment with unlawfully selling and furnishing heroin, unlawfully possessing heroin, and having a prior conviction of a felony offense. Defendant initially filed a motion to quash the indictment but that motion was denied. Defendant ultimately pled guilty to the selling charge and the prior felony charge when the district attorney agreed to drop the possession charge. Defendant argued that the presence of persons other than the witness under interrogation before the grand jury violated Cal. Penal Code § 939. The court found the record of the grand jury proceedings contained ample evidence to support a true bill under the indictment procedure. Because there was no prejudice shown in the alleged errors, a reversal of the indictment was not warranted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment finding defendant guilty on his plea to unlawfully selling and furnishing heroin and to having a prior conviction of a felony offense.

 

1069 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Pitchess v. Superior Court of Los Angeles County


Civ. No. 35274


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


2 Cal. App. 3d 644; 83 Cal. Rptr. 35; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1451



December 16, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The petitions of the real parties in interest for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied February 11, 1970.



DISPOSITION: The petition for peremptory writ of prohibition is granted requiring the respondent court to annul and vacate the orders heretofore made in each of the cases and to make a new and different order in each of said cases denying the motions for preliminary injunctions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sheriff sought a peremptory writ of prohibition in challenge to a decision by respondent Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which issued preliminary injunctions preventing the sheriff from enforcing laws relating to nude entertainment presented by real parties in interest, "bottomless dancing" club owners and performers (club owners).


OVERVIEW: The trial court, after viewing a performance of a nude female dancer at one of the club owners' places of business, signed a preliminary injunction restraining the sheriff and the state from making any physical arrests of the club owners where the basis for the physical arrests was a purported violation of local or state law in that nude entertainment was featured, except upon the condition that a valid warrant of arrest be obtained from a magistrate who was provided with a copy of the injunction and that the issuance of the criminal complaint be based on probable cause. The court characterized the preliminary injunctions as patently ambiguous and ill-defined and held that they exceeded the power of the trial court. The court also held that the club owners had failed to show such irreparable injury as would entitle them to injunctions enjoining criminal prosecutions where the constitutional validity of the statutes involved was unchallenged, because the evidence was not sufficient for the trial court to infer that the motive of the sheriff was interference with freedom of expression rather than law enforcement.


OUTCOME: The court granted the peremptory writ of prohibition, vacated the prior orders, and ordered the trial court to deny the club owners' motions for preliminary injunction.

 

1070 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Muller v. Tanner


Civ. No. 25984


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


2 Cal. App. 3d 445; 82 Cal. Rptr. 738; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1428



December 9, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] On January 6, 1970, the opinion was modified to read as printed above.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, Robert J. Drewes, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The Judgment of Dismissal filed February 20, 1968, is reversed. The case is remanded with directions to grant the plaintiff's pending motions insofar as they seek to vacate the Order Declaring Plaintiff a Vexatious Litigant and for Security filed August 28, 1967, and the minute order of August 7, 1967, upon which it is predicated, and to reset the matter for hearing upon defendant's Motion to Declare Plaintiff a Vexatious Litigant and for Security upon such evidence, written or oral by witnesses or affidavit, including that contained in the declarations now on file, as may be material to the ground of the motion. The Order Setting Aside Default and Entry of Default filed August 16, 1967, is affirmed, without costs to defendant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from a judgment of dismissal of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) entered after his failure to post security, as required by an order that determined he was a vexatious litigant, and ordered him to post $ 5,000 in cash, or bond, within 10 days of the order, pursuant to Cal. Civ. Proc. Code §§ 391- 391.6.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff argued that the vexatious litigant statute was unconstitutional, the showing made by defendant to support the order and the judgment was inadequate, and the propriety of other rulings affected his right to an adequate hearing on the issues raised by the demand for security. The appellate court stated the statute was upheld against many of the grounds of attack raised by plaintiff and that a reading of the language and definitions found therein revealed that his attack was groundless. The court determined that plaintiff acted diligently in requesting a continuance because of his inability to attend two hearings at once and in relying on the reasonable belief that it would be granted. Moreover, plaintiff acted diligently in urging that defendant's motion for security was interposed too late. The fact that the court did not believe him and refused to give him an opportunity to be heard on the merits should not have defeated his right to have the matter reopened when all of the facts were before the court. The court ruled there was no evidence to sustain one of the two proposals, which the order on which it was predicated stood.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that plaintiff's attacks on the constitutionality of the vexatious litigant statute were unwarranted, that there were irregularities which prevented plaintiff from having an adequate hearing on the issues raised by defendant's motion for security, and that the judgment be reversed because the showing made by defendant was inadequate to support the order upon which the judgment was predicated.

People v. Savala


Crim. No. 5227


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


2 Cal. App. 3d 415; 82 Cal. Rptr. 647; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1424



December 8, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Yolo County, Thomas Coakley, Judge. *


* Assigned by the Chairman of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: Judgment is reversed and the cause remanded for the purpose of making the determination as to whether the case is an unusual one within the meaning of the third paragraph of Penal Code section 1203 and thus whether probation shall or shall not be granted, and for resentencing in accordance with the views expressed herein.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his convictions and sentence by the Superior Court of Yolo County (California) for two counts of first-degree robbery and one count of first-degree burglary. Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in convicting him of first-degree robbery, that his counsel was inadequate, that the prosecutor engaged in misconduct, and that he was improperly denied probation under Cal. Penal Code § 1203.


OVERVIEW: When they went outside to investigate noises, a work camp owner's nephew and grandson were grabbed by defendant and another person and taken back into the home office. Defendant had a knife with a six inch blade and the other man had a gun. The grandson was struck several times and tied up. The nephew was held down and a ring was stolen from his pocket. A cash box was also stolen. Both boys identified defendant as the perpetrator. The prosecutor used defendant's statutory rape conviction to impeach his character. The trial court held that it could not sentence defendant to probation without the prosecutor's concurrence. On appeal, the court held that defense counsel's failure to move for a new trial did not render his assistance inadequate because of defendant's waiver and because the case was not close. The court held that although the statutory rape conviction was not a particularly sound basis for impeachment, it was permissible under Cal. Evid. Code § 788 and was not prejudicial. The court held that the trial court should have made a determination under Cal. Penal Code § 1203 as to whether the case was an unusual one and whether or not probation was appropriate on that basis.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for the purpose of making a determination as to whether the case was an unusual one and thus whether probation should or should not be granted to defendant and for resentencing.

 

1072 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Stagg v. Municipal Court for Monica Judicial Dist.


Civ. No. 33898


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


2 Cal. App. 3d 318; 82 Cal. Rptr. 578; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1415; 2 ELR 20083



December 4, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, James G. Whyte, Beach Vasey, and Delbert E. Wong, Judges.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted respondent pilot's petition for a writ of prohibition that restrained respondent municipal court from proceeding with the trial against the pilot for a violation of Santa Monica, Cal., Municipal Code § 10105(a).


OVERVIEW: The pilot was charged with the operation of a jet aircraft that took off from the city airport after 11:00 p.m. and before 7:00 a.m. the next day in violation of § 10105(a). The ordinance existed to alleviate the problem of jet aircraft noise during late night hours. The superior court granted the pilot's petition for a writ of prohibition to restrain the municipal court from proceeding with the trial against him because it determined that § 10105(a) was an unconstitutional attempt to regulate a field that was preempted by federal and state law. The court reversed the superior court's judgment and held that § 10105(a) was valid. The court held that there was no specific state legislation on the subject of noise abatement and that the question of the hours during which the city's airport was to be made available to jet plane takeoffs was not of statewide concern. Also, § 10105(a) did not conflict with existing legislation in the general field of aviation and the subject matter of the ordinance clearly came under the city's power under Cal. Gov't Code § 50474. The ordinance was also upheld as a valid exercise of the city's police power pursuant to Cal. Const. art. XI, § 11.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the superior court's judgment that granted the pilot's request for a writ of prohibition.

People v. Maugh

Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


1 Cal. App. 3d 856; 82 Cal. Rptr. 147; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1334



November 19, 1969

Penal Code § 647a(1). The jury found that defendant was a mentally disordered sex offender, who was not able to benefit by treatment in a state hospital.


OVERVIEW: During his commitment to a state hospital to determine if he was a mentally disordered sex offender, defendant stated that he did not wish treatment. Thereafter, the superintendent of the hospital opined that defendant was a mentally disordered sex offender, but that he was not able to benefit from treatment. The court further held that the superior court's action in returning defendant to the municipal court for further proceedings was proper under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 5512 because the mental hospital opined that defendant was not able to benefit from treatment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

People v. Spearman


Crim. No. 15168


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


1 Cal. App. 3d 898; 82 Cal. Rptr. 277; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1338



November 19, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied January 14, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Charles H. Woodmansee, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted him of committing petty theft after having been convicted of and imprisoned for a felony, a violation of Cal. Penal Code § 667.


OVERVIEW: In an information accusing defendant of the violation of § 667, he was charged with having suffered six previous convictions of felonies for which he had served a period of imprisonment. It was only necessary that one prior be established to invoke the part of § 677 which brought about felony punishment. Defendant was convicted of violating § 677. Defendant appealed his conviction, contending that the statute was unconstitutional, and the court affirmed. The court held that the classification was proper; the court could not say that the Legislature was unreasonable in taking the position that it was more serious for a person who had previously been convicted of a felony (or of petty theft), to again commit petty theft than for a person who has not been so convicted previously to do so. The court held further that defendant's privilege against self-incrimination was not violated by the procedural scheme of § 677 because admitting the priors was not truly an incrimination; it was only conceding the existence of a previously adjudicated circumstance which placed defendant in a heavier punishment category.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1076 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Schindler v. Palo Verde Irrigation Dist.


Civ. No. 9419


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


1 Cal. App. 3d 831; 82 Cal. Rptr. 61; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1332



November 18, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Riverside County, Richard Marsh, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The trial court properly sustained the demurrer to the complaint as amended. Judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner appealed an order of the Superior Court of Riverside County (California), which dismissed his complaint against defendant district seeking a declaration that the voting provision of the Palo Verde Irrigation District Act (Act), 1927 Cal. Stat. ch. 583, § 6, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The landowner filed an action against the district on behalf of himself and other landowners. He claimed that § 6 of the Act, which distributed voting power among landowners in district elections according to the value of their land, violated the equal protection clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. The trial court granted the district's demurrer and dismissed the landowner's complaint without leave to amend. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's order. The court held that § 6 was not unconstitutional because (1) the state had a compelling interest in the reclamation of waste lands through flood protection, drainage, and irrigation works, and (2) the statutory voting formula was necessary to further this compelling interest. The court determined that the grant of franchise in proportion to the value of land ownership fairly distributed voting influence among those primarily and directly interested in direct proportion to the stake each landowner had in the district. The court held that the landowner was not entitled to cumulative voting rights pursuant to Cal. Corp. Code § 2235 because the provision did not apply to the district.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order granting the district's demurrer and dismissing the landowner's complaint in his action challenging the voting provision of the Palo Verde Irrigation District Act.

 

1077 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Fuller v. State


Civ. No. 9364


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


1 Cal. App. 3d 664; 82 Cal. Rptr. 78; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1314



November 12, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied January 8, 1970. Peters, J., and Mosk, J., were of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Imperial County, George R. Kirk, J.



DISPOSITION: The order is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant personal injury victim (victim) sought review of an order from the Superior Court, Imperial County (California), which granted respondent state's motion to dismiss the victim's personal injury action for failure to file an undertaking for costs pursuant to Cal. Gov't Code § 947.


OVERVIEW: The victim alleged that the state's negligent maintenance of a state highway resulted in injuries that rendered her quadriplegic. The trial court granted the state's motion to dismiss because the victim did not file an undertaking within 20 days after service of the state's demand for an undertaking under § 947. The court affirmed the order, concluding that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in dismissing the action. Although the victim claimed indigency, the court found that she did not make a sufficient showing of inability to furnish an undertaking with at least two sufficient sureties pursuant to § 947. The court emphasized the distinction between a showing of inability to furnish security as opposed to a showing of inability to pay accruing fees. Although the victim's affidavit in opposition to the state's motion stated that the victim was indigent and showed the victim's present personal inability to make any payment, it was not sufficient to show an inability to obtain sureties against a future contingency. The court also held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in fixing the amount of the undertaking.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that granted the state's motion to dismiss the victim's personal injury action for failure to file an undertaking for costs.

 

1078 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Berumen


Crim. No. 15283


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


1 Cal. App. 3d 471; 81 Cal. Rptr. 757; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1293



November 5, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Aubrey N. Irwin, J.



DISPOSITION: The order denying motion for new trial 2 is affirmed; the appeal from the nonexistent judgment is dismissed. ( People v. Murphy, 70 Cal.2d 109, 115 [74 Cal.Rptr. 65, 448 P.2d 945].)



2 ( Pen. Code, § 1237, subd. 2, as of February 9, 1968, when notice of appeal was filed.)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which found her guilty of possession of heroin, a violation of Cal. Health & Saf. Code § 11500. The trial court also denied defendant's motions for a new trial and to strike a prior conviction and ordered defendant committed to a rehabilitation center. Defendant appealed the trial court's decision.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried before a jury. The jury became hopelessly deadlocked, and the trial court declared a mistrial. In the second trial, defendant moved to suppress the evidence, pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 1538.5. The trial court denied the motion because it was not timely filed. Defendant's attorney also stipulated that defendant had a prior conviction for a drug violation. In the second trial, the jury convicted defendant. Defendant argued that the trial court should have granted her motion for a new trial because the conduct of her defense counsel had reduced her trial to a sham and a farce. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that: (1) § 1538.5 required defendant to file a motion to suppress the evidence; (2) defendant had 10 days to suppress the evidence before the second trial and had failed to do so; (3) § 1538.5 precluded defendant from raising the issues of probable cause for her arrest and the legality of the ensuing search; and (4) defendant's counsel had stipulated the evidence of the prior conviction, binding defendant to the stipulation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying the motion for new trial and it dismissed the appeal from a nonexistent judgment.

Funke v. Department of Motor Vehicles


Civ. No. 12253


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


1 Cal. App. 3d 449; 81 Cal. Rptr. 662; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1289



November 4, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied December 3, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sacramento County, Gordon D. Schaber, J.



DISPOSITION: As we determine that no clear and mandatory duty to vacate the order is established, the judgment denying the writ is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a driver whose license was suspended pursuant to Cal. Veh. Code § 13353 by respondent, the California Department of Motor Vehicles, sought review of a decision by the Sacramento County Superior Court (California), which denied the driver's application for a writ of mandate to compel the Department to vacate its order.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the driver argued that he had not refused to take the tests for intoxication at the police station but that he wanted to consult his doctor and his attorney first. He argued that the blood test taken by his doctor should have been considered. He claimed that testifying in the Department's administrative hearing prior to his criminal trial impaired his constitutional right against self-incrimination and that he had to disclose his defenses prematurely. Finally, the driver argued that § 13353 was invalid because it provided for the summary suspension of a license upon the sworn statement of an arresting officer. The court held that: (1) the refusal to take the tests at the police station came after his original refusal at the hospital; (2) whether the driver refused to take the tests was a question of fact for the trial court; (3) the blood test taken by the doctor was substantially different in time than when the tests were refused by the driver; (4) the driver did not show that he was prejudiced by testifying in the hearing prior to the trial; and (5) admission of the officer's statement was authorized by Cal. Code Civ. Proc. § 2009.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1080 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Spurlock v. Department of Motor Vehicles


Civ. No. 9207


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


1 Cal. App. 3d 821; 82 Cal. Rptr. 42; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1331



October 31, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of San Bernardino County, A. D. Mitchell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner driver appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of San Bernardino County (California), which held that, pursuant to Cal. Veh. Code § 13353, her driver's license was properly suspended and that she was not entitled to a writ of mandate. Respondent Department of Motor Vehicles opposed the driver's application.


OVERVIEW: After running into a pole, the driver was stopped by a police officer who was aware of the incident and who matched the driver's car to the accident. The police officer smelled alcohol on the driver's breath, and she refused to take a sobriety test. Pursuant to § 13353, she was notified that her license was suspended for six months. A referee, who was not an attorney, held a hearing and found that the suspension of the driver's driving privileges was proper. The driver applied for a writ of mandate from the trial court, and it denied the driver's application. The court affirmed, holding that the police had reasonable cause to stop the driver because the appearance of the car and the damage to the car matched the description of the vehicle that the police had obtained. The driver's arrest was supported by probable cause because the officer smelled alcohol on her breath, and he observed that she was unable to satisfactorily perform roadside sobriety tests. The court ruled that even though referee was not an attorney, referees presiding over implied consent hearings were not required to be attorneys and did not need to comply with the requirements of Cal. Gov't. Code § 11502.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which held that the driver's license was properly suspended and that she was not entitled to a writ of mandate against the Department of Motor Vehicles.

 

1081 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Varanelli v. Structural Pest Control Board


Civ. No. 34063


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


1 Cal. App. 3d 217; 81 Cal. Rptr. 492; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1270



October 28, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied December 17, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Aubrey, N. Irwin, J.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, door-to door salesmen, sought review from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which ruled in favor of defendant, the Structural Pest Control Board, in the salesmen's action contesting the constitutionality of the Structural Pest Control Act (Act), Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 8500-8677, which prohibited door-to-door solicitations for pest control inspections without securing a license.


OVERVIEW: The trial court concluded that the Act covered the solicitations being carried on by the salesmen, that such coverage was constitutional, and that the salesmen were not entitled to conduct door-to-door solicitations for free pest control inspections without securing a license under the Act. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the Act covered door-to-door sales because, by denying a general exemption for all employees and by not granting authority to unlicensed employees to solicit or otherwise secure work, the clear implication of the Act was that unlicensed employees could not solicit or otherwise secure structural pest control work. Further, the court found that the Act, which regulated door-to-door solicitations, was constitutional because there were many rationally acceptable hypotheses for the requirement that a licensed operator perform his own direct contact with owners or hire a licensed field representative to perform that activity. Thus, there was sufficient justification for the legislative action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment upholding the constitutionality Act.

 

1082 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Cohen


Crim. No. 16702


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


1 Cal. App. 3d 94; 81 Cal. Rptr. 503; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1254



October 22, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied November 13, 1969, and appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied December 17 1969. Traynor, C. J. Peters, J. and Tobriner, J., were of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Municipal Court of the Los Angeles Judicial District of Los Angeles County, James Harvey Brown, Judge.



DISPOSITION: In a court trial, the trial judge's erroneous opinion on the law is not grounds for a reversal. ( People v. Wolfe, 257 Cal.App.2d 420, 426 [64 Cal.Rptr. 855].) We have examined each of the points raised by the defendant without finding reversible error. The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Municipal Court of the Los Angeles Judicial District of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted him of willfully and maliciously disturbing the peace in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 415 and sentenced him accordingly.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for disturbing the peace when he wore a jacket with offensive language when he entered the court house while children were present. On appeal, defendant argued that he could not be guilty of the crime because his conduct consisted of the use of words unaccompanied by violence or the threat of violence. The court found that defendant deliberately wore a jacket with language that was clearly offensive and below the minimum standard of propriety and the accepted norm of public behavior. Defendant's conduct was more than a quiet and peaceful assertion of his convictions about the draft. Defendant was not subjected to prosecution for expressing his political beliefs. His right to speak against the draft and war was protected by the First Amendment. However, he did not have the right to express his views by means of printing lewd and vulgar language which was likely to cause others to breach the peace to protect women and children from such exposure. Defendant's conduct in this case went beyond the permissive ambit of the First Amendment's protection.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for disturbing the peace was affirmed.

 

1083 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Dooley's Hardware Mart v. Food Giant Markets, Inc.


Civ. No. 33581


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


1 Cal. App. 3d 105; 81 Cal. Rptr. 451; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1255; 1969 Trade Cas. (CCH) P72,979



October 22, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The petition of respondent Food Giant Markets, Inc., for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied December 17, 1969. Peters, J., was of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Max Z. Wisot, J.



DISPOSITION: The judgement is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a hardware mart, sought review from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which ruled in favor of defendants, a retail food market and two of its employees, in plaintiff's action for an injunction to prevent alleged violations of the California Unfair Practices Act, Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 17000- 17101.


OVERVIEW: Defendants advertised certain products, as to which the food market was in competition with plaintiff, below their cost. Plaintiff sought an injunction to prevent defendants' actions on the basis that their actions violated the California Unfair Practices Act, which prohibited the sale of products below cost when the effect was to injure competitors or destroy competition. Plaintiff relied for proof of the wrongfulness of that conduct on the statutory presumption set forth in Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 17071.5, which stated that selling a product below cost raised a presumption of an intent to injure or destroy a competitor. The trial court ruled that the presumption was unconstitutional and, because there was no other evidence sufficient to support plaintiff's case, judgment was entered for defendants. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the statutory presumption was valid because there was a reasonable relationship between the conduct involved and the fact presumed. There was a rational connection between the limitation of the quantity of goods sold below cost, and any requisite evil intent to justify requiring defendants to prove that they had an honorable intent.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment.

 

1084 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


United California Bank v. People


Civ. No. 33211


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


1 Cal. App. 3d 1; 81 Cal. Rptr. 405; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1244



October 20, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied November 4, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Julian Beck, J., plaintiff was awarded damages.



DISPOSITION: Judgment for plaintiff is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, Department of Public Works (Department), sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted respondent bank, as trustee for a retail department store, a judgment of $ 54,625 in an inverse condemnation suit.


OVERVIEW: Work done by the Department (1) closed old First Street where it abutted the bank's store and (2) relocated First Street to the north, (3) required southbound vehicles intending to visit the store to use an up-curving ramp in order to turn into new First Street and thence into a new parking lot, and (4) impaired the view of the store including its display window. On appeal, the court determined that the Department's works of improvement interfered with the store's rights of access and exposure. An actionable interference was established. Contrary to the Department's contention, the trial court did not err in holding the liberation of Old First Street for parking could not be considered in evaluating special benefits. Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1248(3) limited special benefits to those arising from the construction and improvement proposed. Here, the development of parking was no part of the Department's work; hence, the development could not constitute a special benefit. Finally, the trial court did not err prejudicially in instructing the jury that the store's rights were substantially impaired. Under Cal. Evid. Code § 310, all questions of law were to be decided by the court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for the bank.

 

1085 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


ST. LOUIS-SAN FRANCISCO RY. CO. v. SUPERIOR COURT OF LOS ANGELES CTY.


Civ. No. 34663


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


276 Cal. App. 2d 762; 81 Cal. Rptr. 705; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1863



October 10, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Petition of the Real Parties in Interest for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 3, 1969. Mosk, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING in mandamus to compel the Superior Court of Los Angeles County to dismiss a civil action.



DISPOSITION: Peremptory writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant railroad sought a mandamus to compel the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) to vacate its order denying the railroad's motion to dismiss because of a failure to comply with Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 583.


OVERVIEW: A railroad train, owned and operated by the railroad, and an automobile operated by plaintiff motorist, were involved in a collision where plaintiff passenger was injured. A personal injury action was filed by plaintiffs in California in the respondent trial court. At the conclusion of the trial verdict was directed in favor of the railroad. An appeal was taken and the judgment was reversed. The railroad filed a notice of motion to dismiss arguing that under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 583 dismissal was mandatory because of the failure of plaintiffs to bring the matter to trial within three years after the filing of the remittitur. The trial court denied the railroad's motion. The railroad sought a mandamus to compel the trial court to vacate its order denying the railroad's motion to dismiss. The court held that plaintiffs failed to comply with the three-year limitation of § 583 and found to be the appropriate law rather than the 10-year provision of the Arkansas law that plaintiffs claimed applied. Since no evidence was presented which would demonstrate that there was compliance with § 583, the court held that the trial judge erred in denying the railroad's motion for a dismissal.


OUTCOME: The court granted the railroad's request for a mandamus to compel the trial court to vacate its order denying the railroad's motion to dismiss plaintiffs' action.

 

1086 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Estate of Kraemer


Civ. No. 33843


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


276 Cal. App. 2d 715; 81 Cal. Rptr. 287; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1857



October 9, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 3, 1969. Peters, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Joseph L. Call, Judge.

Action to determine heirship to an estate.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment determining petitioner to be sole heir affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claimant state appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which determined that petitioner foreign national was the sole heir of the decedent, who was a California resident, and that she was entitled to the decedent's whole estate, which consisted of real and personal property.


OVERVIEW: The foreign national was a citizen and resident of East Germany. After the decedent's death, the foreign national filed an action to determine heirship to his estate. The trial court entered a judgment that found that the foreign national was the sole heir of the decedent and that she was entitled to distribution of the whole estate. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and held that Cal. Prob. Code § 259 was an intrusion by the state into the field of foreign affairs that the United States Constitution entrusted to the President and the Congress. The court determined that no treaty governed the rights to succession to the decedent's personal property, thus, the disposition or the right of succession was governed by the laws of California. Under California law, the foreign national was entitled to a full distribution of the decedent's estate and the state was not entitled to any right or title therein or distribution thereof. The decedent left neither issue nor a spouse, thus, under Cal. Prob. Code § 225, his estate went to the foreign national as the decedent's surviving parent. Cal. Prob. Code § 1026 authorized the foreign national to demand the estate property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which held that the foreign national was entitled to the decedent's whole estate.

 

1087 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Mandel v. Municipal Court for Oakland-Piedmont Judicial Dist.


Civ. No. 26042


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


276 Cal. App. 2d 649; 81 Cal. Rptr. 173; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1851



October 8, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Petition of the Real Party in Interest and Respondent for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 3, 1969. Burke, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Alameda County. Frederick M. Van Sicklen, Judge.

Proceeding in prohibition to restrain a municipal court from proceeding with a pending criminal action charging vagrancy.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment denying writ reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner accused appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Alameda County (California), which denied his writ of prohibition to restrain respondent municipal court and the real party in interest, the state, from proceeding with a pending criminal action in which the accused was charged with five counts of vagrancy in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 653g, which the accused alleged was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The accused handed out anti-draft leaflets at a school, which gave notice of a student meeting. The accused was arrested and filed a demurrer to stop the state from prosecuting him under § 653g. The trial court overruled the demurrer that the municipal court lacked jurisdiction. The accused entered a plea of not guilty and commenced an action for a writ of prohibition. The writ was denied. The accused appealed. The court reversed and granted the writ. Section 653g was not constitutionally invalid because it was construed to apply only to loitering for the purpose of committing a crime. Because facts alleged in the complaint showed that the accused was lawfully handing out leaflets, there was no public offense under § 653g. The facts did not support loitering to contribute to the delinquency of a minor in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 272 because the leaflet urged attendance at a meeting, but not during school hours. Even if it had, a one-day absence was not habitual truancy. Because the charge was not contained in the indictment, it violated due process. The state's construction of § 653g violated the First and Fourteenth Amendments because it was content based.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's denial of the demurrer and remanded the matter with directions to comply with the writ of prohibition issued by the court.

Koop v. Structural Pest Control Board


Civ. No. 33008


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


276 Cal. App. 2d 249; 81 Cal. Rptr. 154; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1799



September 19, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Benjamin B. Ostrin, Court Commissioner, Judge pro tem.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the Structural Pest Control Board to reinstate the licenses of a field representative and an operator and to direct the registrar not to require a restoration bond.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part with directions. Judgment denying writ affirmed as to operator's license, and reversed with directions as to field representative's license and bond.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, pest control field representative licensee and operator licensee, sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied their petitions in mandamus to compel appellee state structural pest control board to reinstate their licenses and to direct the registrar not to require a restoration bond.


OVERVIEW: Appellants argued the unconstitutionality of certain laws and regulations relevant to the infractions for which their licenses were revoked. They also argued that the orders suspending the field representative's license for 15 days and the operator's license for 180 days, subject to three years' probation and a 30-day suspension, were harsh, arbitrary, and not in the furtherance of duty. They claimed that the requirement for restoration bonds was an abuse of discretion. The court agreed with the board's position that appellants' points were neither sufficiently relevant nor were their authorities sufficiently germane to be persuasive. In the absence of a clear and convincing demonstration that the challenged provisions of the act were arbitrary or were incapable of furthering a lawful purpose under the police power, the court found them constitutional. In light of the fact that the operator made double infractions and had a previous violation, the court held that the requirement of a restoration bond within the statutory limits was not an abuse of discretion. However, the court held that the requirement of a restoration bond from the field representative must be reconsidered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment as to the operator. The judgment was reversed as to the field representative, and the trial court was instructed to issue a peremptory writ of mandate directing the board to set aside its order suspending the field representative's license and to reconsider the penalty imposed and to reconsider the matter of the representative's restoration bond.

Bethlehem Steel Corp. v. Bd. of Comm'ns


Civ. Nos. 32969, 32976


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


276 Cal. App. 2d 221; 80 Cal. Rptr. 800; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1795



September 18, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 12, 1969. Mosk, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Robert W. Kenny, Judge.

Actions for injunctions to prevent a city's water and power department from performing a contract awarded to a bidder using foreign steel and from awarding a certain contract to any competitive bidder using foreign steel.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Summary judgments for defendants affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, plaintiff steel company sought review of summary judgments from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), rendered in actions denying it injunctive relief and damages against defendant water and power department. The steel company sought injunctions to prevent the department from performing a contract awarded to a bidder using foreign steel under the California Buy American Act, Cal. Gov't Code §§ 4300-4305.


OVERVIEW: The Act required that contracts for the construction of public works or the purchase of materials for public use be awarded only to persons who agreed to use or supply materials, which have been manufactured in the United States, substantially all from materials produced in the United States. The issue presented on appeal was whether the Act violated the United States Constitution. The court concluded that the Act was an unconstitutional encroachment upon the federal government's exclusive power over foreign affairs, and constituted an undue interference with the United States' conduct of foreign relations. The court found that the Act, in effectively placing an embargo on foreign products, amounted to usurpation by the state of the power of the federal government to conduct foreign trade policy. Furthermore, the court found that the Act amounted to an attempt by the state to structure national foreign policy to conform to its own domestic policies. Therefore, the court concluded that the Act was an unconstitutional intrusion into an exclusive federal domain.


OUTCOME: The summary judgments entered in favor of the department were affirmed.

Noonan v. Green


Civ. No. 11813


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


276 Cal. App. 2d 25; 80 Cal. Rptr. 513; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1767

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Siskiyou County. Frank S. Petersen, Judge. *


* Assigned by the Chairman of the Judicial Council.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel a high school district and its board members to set aside and vacate an order requiring female students to wear uniforms and to set aside the suspension of one student.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment granting writ reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant school officials appealed the decision of the Superior Court of Siskiyou County (California), which granted a writ of mandamus to plaintiff student to compel the school officials to set aside and vacate an order requiring female students to wear uniforms and to set aside the suspension of the student.


OVERVIEW: A high school required all female students to wear uniform style dress four days a week. The student refused to wear the proscribed dress and was suspended. The school officials scheduled a hearing before the school board, but the student filed for a writ of mandamus in the trial court before the hearing. McDaniel v. McDaniel


Civ. No. 33112


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


275 Cal. App. 2d 927; 80 Cal. Rptr. 837; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 2000



August 28, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied September 25, 1969, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 22, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Orlando H. Rhodes, Judge.

Action for damages for alleged misrepresentation of community property assets at the time of a divorce property settlement agreement and for declaratory relief.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiff awarding general and exemplary damages affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant husband appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) that granted plaintiff wife general damages, exemplary damages, and attorneys' fees, in an action for alleged misrepresentations by the husband to the wife in connection with a property settlement agreement in an action for divorce.


OVERVIEW: The parties entered into a property settlement agreement in conjunction with their divorce. The husband submitted a financial statement that summarized his assets and liabilities as of a certain date. He then exchanged common shares for preferred shares and borrowed shares to exchange. Later he exchanged the preferred shares for convertible preference stock. The wife alleged misrepresentation of community property at the time of the settlement and asked for declaratory relief. The husband argued the evidence did not support the findings and the damages were excessive. The court ruled that the evidence supported the findings that the representations and concealments of the husband were false, that he fraudulently induced the wife's counsel to make the agreement effective as of a certain date in order to cover up and conceal the fraud, and that, by reason of fraudulent concealments and representations, and by reason of the retention of the additional preferred shares, the husband became a constructive trustee for the benefit of the wife of one-half of the additional shares. There was no error in awarding general damages and no abuse of discretion in awarding exemplary damages.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1093 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Harriman v. Beverly Hills


Civ. No. 33594


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


275 Cal. App. 2d 918; 80 Cal. Rptr. 426; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1999; 35 A.L.R.3d 1421



August 27, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 22, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Lloyd S. Davis, Judge.

Action to prevent a city from enforcing an ordinance for the licensing of telephone answering services.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying injunction and upholding ordinance affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff answering service owners brought suit against defendant city, arguing that an ordinance regulating answering services was unconstitutional and seeking injunctive relief. The Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) entered judgment in favor of defendant. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: After a vice squad investigated a purported conspiracy between prostitutes and telephone answering services, defendant adopted an ordinance requiring that operators of such services obtain a permit and that permit applicants and their employees be investigated and fingerprinted. The court affirmed the trial court's decision. It rejected the argument that the ordinance was arbitrary because other businesses were not affected, stating that defendant could confine its restrictions to those classes of cases where the need for regulation was deemed to be clearest. Moreover, it held, in considering the ordinance, it was to be presumed that defendant made inquiry to determine whether there was an evil to be remedied and that the classification recognized in the ordinance was the result of such an inquiry. It held that defendant's determination to regulate only services inside its limits was not so palpably unreasonable and arbitrary as to be discriminatory. Finally, it held that the ordinance was not an unreasonable exercise of defendant's police power, noting that the state required applicants for various other licenses, credentials, or jobs to be fingerprinted or photographed.


OUTCOME: In plaintiff's' action challenging the constitutionality of defendant's ordinance regulating answering services, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of defendant.

Bone v. State Board of Cosmetology


Civ. No. 33194


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


275 Cal. App. 2d 851; 80 Cal. Rptr. 164; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1991



August 26, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 22, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Ralph H. Nutter, Judge.

Action to enjoin the State Board of Cosmetology from enforcing a statute which provides that a cosmetologist's license does not authorize the holder to cut hair in an establishment which is primarily a barbershop.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal after demurrer was sustained without leave to amend affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff licensed cosmetologist appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which dismissed his action for an injunction brought against defendants, State Board of Barber Examiners and State Board of Cosmetology, in an action brought under the Barber Law, Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 6500 et seq., and the Cosmetology Act, Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 7300 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The cosmetologist operated two establishments which specialized in the styling and cutting of men's hair. The cosmetologist argued that defendants had threatened to enforce Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 6522 against him and would thereby force him to discontinue his business unless defendants were enjoined from doing so. On appeal, the cosmetologist also argued that § 6522 as amended in 1967 was unconstitutional. The court affirmed, concluding that (1) it was not unreasonable for the legislature to say that, although cosmetologists could cut hair in the course of their broader practice of cosmetology, an establishment which was engaged primarily in the business of haircutting had to use those who were trained and registered as barbers; (2) the statute was discriminatory only in the sense that any licensing system discriminated by making specified activity lawful only for those persons who qualify for and obtained a license; and (3) there being a reasonable basis for the limitation, no invidious denial of equal protection was involved.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which denied the cosmetologist's action for an injunction brought against the state board of barber examiners and state board of cosmetology.

People v. Wright


Crim. Nos. 15095, 15346


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


275 Cal. App. 2d 738; 80 Cal. Rptr. 335; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1975



August 20, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALS from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County and from an order of commitment. Mark Brandler, Judge.

Prosecution for possession of marijuana.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; appeal from order dismissed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial, the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) entered a judgment that found defendant guilty of possession of marijuana in violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11530. During hearings on his alleged violation of probation, defendant was ordered committed to the state department of corrections for a diagnostic study under Cal. Penal Code § 1203.3. After his probation was revoked, defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Upon his conviction for marijuana possession, defendant was placed on probation for a period of five years. One condition of defendant's probation provided as follows: Do not publicly or privately by words or conduct urge or advocate, encourage, or solicit others to use or possess any narcotics or psychedelic drugs. Defendant's probation was revoked because he allegedly advocated violation of the narcotic laws. Defendant appealed his conviction and probation revocation. The court dismissed defendant's appeal from the order of commitment because it was not an appealable order. Noting that defendant's freedom of religion objection to the constitutionality of § 11530 and its companion sections previously had been considered and denied, the court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court then held that the probation condition did not violate defendant's constitutional right of free speech because it only prohibited the advocacy of violation of the narcotic laws so long as they were in force, and it was that advocacy, not political argument, that defendant was found to have made.


OUTCOME: After dismissing defendant's appeal from an order of commitment for a diagnostic study, the court affirmed defendant's conviction and the revocation of his probation.

 

1096 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Imperial Termite Control, Inc. v. Structural Pest Control Board


Civ. No. 33181


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


275 Cal. App. 2d 685; 80 Cal. Rptr. 156; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1966



August 19, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 15, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Ralph H. Nutter, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the Structural Pest Control Board to set aside its disciplinary order suspending licenses for ten days.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant structural pest control licensee sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which sustained the action of respondent California Structural Pest Control Board that suspended the licensee's license for a period of 10 days and refused to issue an order to enjoin that suspension.


OVERVIEW: Following an administrative hearing the Board suspended the licensee's structural pest control license for a period of 10 days. The licensee sought administrative mandamus, but the superior court refused to issue an order that enjoined the suspension. The licensee appealed and the court affirmed, finding that the supplementary regulations promulgated by the Board did not exceed its rulemaking authority created by Cal. Gov't. Code § 11374. The regulations of the Board that resulted in the licensee's suspension did not violate its equal protection rights because the climatic and geological conditions of California were conducive to wood-destroying pests and organisms and regulations to protect property owners from ignorant, incompetent, or dishonest pest control operators were within the authority of the legislature to permit. The court was without power to review the extent of the penalty imposed by the Board because it was within the legislatively set limits under Cal Bus. & Prof. Code § 8697.3. The activity by the licensee that gave rise to its suspension was within that covered by the Board's regulations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that sustained the action of the Board in suspending the licensee's license for a period of 10 days and the refusal to issue an order to enjoin that suspension.

People v. Superior Court of Butte County


Civ. No. 12224


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


275 Cal. App. 2d 489; 79 Cal. Rptr. 904; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1940



August 7, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitioner's Application for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 1, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING in mandamus to compel the Superior Court of Butte County to annul an order suppressing certain evidence in a prosecution for possession of marijuana.



DISPOSITION: Writ denied; order to show cause discharged and temporary stay terminated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The People brought a proceeding in mandamus to compel respondent Superior Court of Butte County (California) to annul an order suppressing certain evidence in a prosecution for possession of marijuana.


OVERVIEW: A United States postman was delivering mail when he opened a bundle of mail to put it into his satchel, a first-class package fell out onto the seat of his car. When the package fell out on the seat the outside wrapping came apart, as did a box wrapped in it, and a brown paper bag fell out of the box. The postman opened the bag and saw what turned out to be out to be marijuana. A search warrant was issued and evidence seized. Real party in interest was charged in an information filed in the superior court with the crime of possession of marijuana. The real party in interest filed a motion to suppress evidence, which was granted. The superior court judge found that the marijuana in question was not accidentally discovered, but was discovered by an act in clear violation of the federal statutes and postal regulations protecting the privacy of first-class parcels and letters. The people appealed pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 1538.5(o). The court denied the people's writ and held that the opening of the bag was a search. The court held that the prosecution failed to show legal justification for the postman's search.


OUTCOME: The court denied the people's requested writ to compel the superior court to annul an order suppressing certain evidence in a prosecution for possession of marijuana. The court discharged the order to show cause and terminated the temporary stay.

 

1098 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hardy


Crim. No. 15915


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


275 Cal. App. 2d 469; 79 Cal. Rptr. 801; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1937



August 6, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied August 27, 1969, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 1, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Aubrey N. Irwin, Judge.

Prosecution for grand theft.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) entered a judgment that convicted defendant of grand theft in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 487.1. Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with grand theft for unlawfully stealing the personal property of another of a value in excess of $ 200. Defendant and a co-defendant allegedly engaged in a bunco operation that relieved an individual of his money and in place thereof left him a wad of paper with a dollar bill wrapped around it in a sack. Defendant and the co-defendant testified that they had played craps with the alleged victim for several months prior to their arrest and that the victim and the co-defendant had gotten into an argument over a dice game in which the victim had lost considerable money. The victim testified that he had never seen defendants prior to the incident in question and that only two months before that he had been in Vietnam. Defendant challenged his conviction. The court held that there was more than sufficient evidence to convict defendant. Defendant also waived any issue concerning the victim's in-court identification. Lastly, Cal. Penal Code § 1025, which required the presentation of evidence of defendant's prior convictions at the same time that proof of the substantive crime was presented, did not deprive defendant of his constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1099 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


In re Valenzuela


Civ. No. 12158, Crim. No. 5183


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


275 Cal. App. 2d 483; 79 Cal. Rptr. 760; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1939



August 6, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 1, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Sacramento County, sitting as a juvenile court, extending the jurisdiction of the California Youth Authority for a period of two years, and PROCEEDING in habeas corpus to secure release from custody. Robert W. Cole and Irving H. Perluss, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed; writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), sitting as a juvenile court, extending the jurisdiction of the California Youth Authority over defendant for a period of two years under the provisions of Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 1800. Defendant also sought a writ of habeas corpus to secure his release from custody.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was 24 years old, was committed to the Authority in 1960 as a result of charges that he had sexually molested an 11-year-old girl. The court held that: (1) at the time of the original commitment, Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 1769 provided that every person committed to the Authority by a juvenile court had to be discharged upon the expiration of a two-year period of control or when the person reached his 21st first birthday, whichever occurred later; (2) Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 1800, which was added in 1963, permitted the period of a person's detention to be extended where his discharge from control of the Authority was physically dangerous to the public; (3) the prohibition against ex post facto laws applied only to punitive and criminal matters; (4) the court could not regard this legislation as being civil rather than criminal because it was penal in nature and effect; and (5) the argument that the challenged statutes were not ex post facto because defendant was confined because of subsequent offenses rather than the antecedent offense failed because the initial offense was the original and indispensable link in the chain of circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order and granted defendant a writ of habeas corpus.

 

1100 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Department of Public Works v. County of Santa Clara


Civ. No. 25947


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


275 Cal. App. 2d 372; 79 Cal. Rptr. 787; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1927



August 1, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied August 28, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County determining that the county tax stamp ordinance does not impose a tax on the recordation of a final order in a condemnation proceeding. Stanley R. Evans, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), which determined that the county tax stamp ordinance did not impose a tax on the recordation of a final order in a condemnation proceeding, and that respondent state was entitled to have the final order recorded without payment of the tax by the condemnee because it was not a sale of realty within the meaning of Cal. Rev. & Tax Code § 11911.


OVERVIEW: The state brought a condemnation proceeding in which the trial court had entered a final order of condemnation. The recorder refused to record the certified copy of the order because the documentary stamp tax imposed by a county ordinance had not been paid. The state then moved for an order requiring the recorder to record the certified copy of the order. The trial court found that the recorder had the duty to accept the order for recordation without requiring the payment of the tax by the condemnee, and held that the final order of the court following a condemnation trial was not a sale of realty within the meaning of Cal. Rev. & Tax Code § 11911. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the ordinance did not mention final orders in condemnation proceedings. The court found that neither the ordinance nor the enabling legislation limited the applicability of the legislation to "voluntary" as opposed to "involuntary" sales. The court found that the recorder must record a final order in a condemnation proceeding properly presented to him pursuant to the provisions of Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1253 without the payment of the transfer tax provided for in the county ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's holding that the recorder had the duty to accept the order for recordation without requiring the payment of the tax by the condemnee because a final order of condemnation was not a sale of realty under the applicable statute and county ordinance.

 

1101 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Jessin v. County of Shasta


Civ. No. 12027


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


274 Cal. App. 2d 737; 79 Cal. Rptr. 359; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 2107; 35 A.L.R.3d 1433



July 11, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Shasta County. Richard W. Abbe, Judge.

Action for a determination that a county is required by law to furnish surgical sterilization without charge if requested by certain indigents.



DISPOSITION: Modified and affirmed. Judgment for plaintiffs modified and affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Shasta County (California), which found in favor of respondent indigents in their action for a determination that the county was required by law to furnish surgical sterilization without charge if requested by them or others similarly situated.


OVERVIEW: The indigents requested the county furnish them with voluntary surgical sterilization. The county refused to furnish the service, claiming the rendering of such services would be unlawful. The trial court declared that voluntary nontherapeutic surgical sterilization was legal in the state and authorized the county to perform such operations upon willing qualified medical indigents, including plaintiffs. The court affirmed the finding that nontherapeutic sterilization was lawful in California where competent consent was given, as there was no public policy prohibiting consensual sterilization operations. The court further found that the trial court rendered judgment on questions bearing upon the scope of medical care under publicly sponsored welfare programs; however, there was no evidence on those issues. It held that, as there was no controversy on those issues, it was an abuse of discretion to render judgment on those questions and modified the judgment to reflect that voluntary non-therapeutic surgical sterilization operations were legal in the state of California and deleted the remainder of the declaratory portion of the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding in favor of the indigents and against the county that nontherapeutic sterilization was lawful in the state. It deleted that portion of the declaratory judgment that bore on the scope of medical care under publicly sponsored welfare programs and affirmed the trial court's judgment as modified.
