In re J.F.


Crim. No. 13349


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


268 Cal. App. 2d 761; 74 Cal. Rptr. 464; 1969 Cal. App. LEXIS 1737



January 13, 1969  
January 13, 1969


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County directing that a minor remain subject to Youth Authority control beyond his twenty-first year. Donald A. Odell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant minor sought review from an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which directed that the minor to remain subject to Youth Authority control beyond age 21.


OVERVIEW: The minor was a ward of the juvenile court and on probation, but failed to comply. After a hearing at which minor was not represented by counsel, he was committed to the Youth Authority. Sometime thereafter the minor was paroled but while on parole again got into trouble. A subsequent Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 1800 hearing was held, where minor was represented by counsel, and the trial court made a finding that the discharge of the minor would have been physically dangerous to the public because of his mental deficiency, disorder and abnormality. The petition was granted and an appeal followed. The trial court entered an order directing the minor to remain subject to Youth Authority control beyond age 21. On review, the court affirmed and held that the findings were adequate in the § 1800 proceeding and that counsel did not raise the issue of the constitutional validity of the prior commitments for lack of counsel. The court held that the "preponderance of the evidence" standard was proper in a § 1800 proceeding because the involuntary confinement was not meant to punish juveniles as in criminal proceedings and the standard did not deprive the minor of equal protection of the law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which directed that the minor remain subject to Youth Authority control beyond age 21.

 

1139 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


County of Alameda v. Aberle


Civ. No. 25099


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Four


268 Cal. App. 2d 424; 73 Cal. Rptr. 926; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1323



December 23, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 19, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Alameda County. Robert L. Bostick, Judge.

Action by a county to recoup welfare benefits and for calculation of an adult child's liability for benefits paid to indigent parents.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiff affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant adult son challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Alameda County (California) entered in favor of respondent county on its complaint for reimbursement for old age security payments made to the son's mother. Under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code §§ 12100 and 12101, formerly Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code §§ 2224 and 2181, the county sought to recoup welfare benefits and for calculation of the son's liability for benefits paid to his parents.


OVERVIEW: The trial court had allocated responsibility for the indigent parents between each spouse. On appeal, the son did not assert that the decision from the trial court was contrary to California law. Rather, the son argued that Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code §§ 12100 and 12101, formerly Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code §§ 2224 and 2181, was invalid in that it deprived married women of vested property rights and unconstitutionally discriminated between married men and married women, in violation of their Fourteenth Amendment right to the equal protection of the laws. The court held that: (1) under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code §§ 12100 and 12101, formerly Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code §§ 2224 and 2181, the treatment of the husband's liability to the county for the support of his indigent parents was in harmony with the State's community property laws; (2) community property, except for the earnings of the wife, was liable for all of the husband's debts; (3) the enactment of Cal. Civ. Code § 161a creating the wife's vested interest did not affect this rule; and (4) there was nothing unfair or discriminatory in the statutory allocation of responsibility for each spouse's indigent parents.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for the county entered by the trial court.

 

1140 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Jones-Hamilton Co. v. Franchise Tax Board


Civ. No. 24672


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


268 Cal. App. 2d 343; 73 Cal. Rptr. 896; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1314



December 20, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] On January 20, 1969, the Opinion was Modified to Read as Printed Above.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Joseph Karesh, Judge.

Action to recover certain corporation taxes paid, plus legal interest.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Summary judgment for defendant affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of the decision of the Superior court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant tax board in the taxpayer's action brought to have recovered an amount it claimed it was owed as a refund.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer argued that a statute passed was void and violative of Cal. Const. art. XIII, § 16 because it was passed by fewer than two-thirds of the members elected to the Senate. The court affirmed the summary judgment. The court held that there was no triable issue of fact and the only issue was one strictly of law. The court determined that the legislation in question was not passed in violation of the California constitution. The presumption was in favor of the constitutionality of the statute and the invalidity of an act of the legislature must have been clear and unquestionable before the statute would have been declared unconstitutional. The statute did not as a matter of law levy a tax in violation of the California constitution and therefore the trial court was justified in granting the tax board's motion. The payment made by the taxpayer was merely an advance payment of a portion of what its estimated tax would have been.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment granted in favor of the tax board in the taxpayer's action for a refund.

Pain v. Municipal Court of San Francisco


Civ. No. 25178


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


268 Cal. App. 2d 151; 73 Cal. Rptr. 862; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1285



December 13, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied January 10, 1969, and the Petition of Plaintiff and Respondent for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 5, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Robert J. Drewes, Judge.

Proceeding in prohibition to restrain the Municipal Court of the City and County of San Francisco from proceeding with a prosecution for committing a public nuisance.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment granting peremptory writ reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The people appealed an order of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) that granted a peremptory writ of prohibition to defendant restraining the municipal court from proceeding with a prosecution of defendant for committing a public nuisance.


OVERVIEW: A complaint was filed in the municipal court alleging that defendant maintained and committed a public nuisance by unlawfully obstructing the free passage and use in the customary manner of a public street. The complaint charged violation of Cal. Penal Code § 370. The municipal court overruled defendant's demurrer to the compliant. Defendant sought prohibition in the superior court, which granted the peremptory writ on the ground that the statute was unconstitutional. The court held that, insofar as it defined the offense charged in the complaint, § 370 was neither vague, uncertain, nor overbroad. It followed that the municipal court properly overruled the demurrer, and the superior court erred in issuing the writ of prohibition.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that issued a writ of prohibition restraining the municipal court from proceeding with a prosecution of defendant for committing a public nuisance.

Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control v. Superior Court of Orange County


Civ. No. 9282


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


268 Cal. App. 2d 67; 73 Cal. Rptr. 780; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1274



December 10, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PROCEEDING in prohibition to direct the Superior Court of Orange County to vacate an order staying enforcement of a liquor license suspension order issued by the Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control.



DISPOSITION: Peremptory writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control brought a proceeding in prohibition to direct respondent Superior Court of Orange County (California) to vacate an order staying enforcement of a liquor license suspension order issued by the department. The ex parte order was obtained by the real parties in interest, found by the department to have violated laws relating to the sale of liquor to minors.


OVERVIEW: The department found that the real parties in interest had violated certain provisions of the Alcoholic Beverage Control Act relating to the sale of liquor to minors and ordered a license suspension. The real parties in interest filed a petition for writ of mandate in the lower court. The lower court dismissed the petition, but the real parties in interest obtained an ex parte order from another judge to restrain the department from enforcing its suspension order pending an appeal from the order dismissing the petition for writ of mandate. The department sought to have that stay order vacated by writ of prohibition. The court found that, under Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 23090.5, the lower court was without jurisdiction to review the final order of the board or to stay enforcement of the suspension order. The court considered the argument of the real parties in interest that § 23090.5 was unconstitutional in that it precluded superior courts from reviewing the validity of an administrative determination. The court rejected the argument because the section did not totally impair the right of judicial review. The court granted the writ of prohibition.


OUTCOME: The court granted the peremptory writ of prohibition sought by the department.

 

1143 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Dixon v. Municipal Court of San Francisco


Civ. No. 24685


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Four


267 Cal. App. 2d 789; 73 Cal. Rptr. 587; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1451



December 2, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied December 23, 1968, and Respondents' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 29, 1969. Peters, J., Tobriner, J., and Mosk, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco granting a writ of prohibition forbidding the municipal court from further prosecuting theatrical performers for "lewd and dissolute conduct in a public place." Joseph Karesh, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant municipal court sought review of an order from the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which granted a writ of prohibition forbidding the municipal court from further prosecuting respondent theatrical performers for lewd and dissolute conduct in a public place under Cal. Penal Code § 647(a).


OVERVIEW: The theatrical performers were charged in the municipal court with violating § 647(a) for simulating an oral sex act in a play. The next level court issued a writ of prohibition forbidding the municipal court from further prosecuting the performers. Upon review the court reversed the order granting the writ, holding that § 647(a) was not unconstitutional for vagueness. The court held that § 647(a) applied to plays and that the municipal court had to determine whether the act was obscene in context with the whole performance, judged by standards of the State of California as a whole, upon consideration of expert testimony.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting the writ of prohibition forbidding the municipal court from further prosecuting the theatrical performers for lewd and dissolute conduct in a public place.

Jordan v. County of Los Angeles

The court found that the appeal was to be dismissed as moot due to the new enactments because the action was originally based upon a justiciable controversy and could not be maintained on appeal where the issue became moot.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal as moot.

 

1145 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Saunders v. Carr


Civ. No. 32773


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


268 Cal. App. 2d 10; 74 Cal. Rptr. 147; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1268



November 20, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 15, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Barbara County. W. Preston Butcher, Judge.

Action for declaratory relief seeking determination that certain provisions of a municipal ordinance are invalid.



DISPOSITION: Judgment modified and affirmed. Judgment for defendant modified to decree that plaintiffs are not entitled to a declaration in their favor, and as so modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Barbara County (California), which dismissed their action for declaratory relief against respondents, city, city council, and parking commission. Plaintiff sought to have certain provisions of an assessment district off-street parking procedure ordinance declared invalid and unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendants passed an ordinance to provide for issuance of bonds to pay the costs of acquiring parking places and for payment of the bonds and interest from ad valorem assessments and parking revenues. The taxpayers sought to have the provisions declared invalid, claiming that the issuance of the bonds was illegal and void. The trial court sustained the defendants' general demurrer without leave to amend and granted their motion to dismiss. The court concluded that the trial court erred in granting the motion to dismiss; however, none of taxpayers' contentions had merit. As such, rather than a judgment of dismissal, the trial court should have entered its judgment decreeing expressly that the taxpayers were not entitled to the declarations they sought. Accordingly, the judgment of the trial court was modified by striking references to the motion to dismiss and inserting in lieu thereof a provision that the ordinance did not violate and was not prohibited by the federal and state constitution and the city charter and that the bonds issued were not null and void and were valid as against the contentions of the taxpayers.


OUTCOME: The court modified the form of the decree to expressly provide that the taxpayers were not entitled to a declaration that the ordinance was void and, as modified, affirmed the judgment.

 

1146 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Turner


Crim. No. 14531


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


267 Cal. App. 2d 440; 73 Cal. Rptr. 263; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1407; 38 A.L.R.3d 940



November 18, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied December 4, 1968, and Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 15, 1969. McComb, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Kenneth A. White, Judge.

Prosecution for grand theft.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment of conviction reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted appellant of grand theft of a rental car and a credit card in violation Cal. Pen. Code § 487(3). Respondent government argued that appellant acted with specific intent in violation of Cal. Pen. Code § 484 (b)(c).


OVERVIEW: Appellant entered into a written contract with a car agency rental of a car and made a cash deposit, but gave a false name and identification. Appellant was arrested while in possession of the car. The owner of the credit card testified that his credit card had been stolen and that he never gave appellant permission to use the card or identification. Appellant testified that he used the false identification because he believed he could not rent the car on his own identification. Appellant testified that he never intended to steal, that he intended to return it on the morning when it was due, and that he intended to pay. On review, appellant contended that the evidence did not support the verdict on the ground that there was no evidence of a specific intent to deprive the owners of their property wholly and permanently. The government argued that Cal. Pen. Code § 484(b)(c) created a presumption of fraud. The court reversed, concluding that: (1) appellant did not act with specific intent to steal when he rented the car using the false identification; and (2) § 484(b)(c) did not create a presumption of fraud because it was not in effect at the time the crime was committed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction for grant theft of a rental car and a credit card.

 

1147 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


West Romaine Corp. v. California State Board of Pharmacy


Civ. No. 31930


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


266 Cal. App. 2d 901; 72 Cal. Rptr. 569; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1583



October 29, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied November 25, 1968, and Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 24, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Edmund M. Moor, Judge. *


* Assigned by the Chairman of the Judicial Council.

Proceeding in administrative mandamus to review disciplinary action of the California State Board of Pharmacy against a retail drug corporation.



DISPOSITION: Modified and affirmed. Judgment granting writ modified as to penalties and affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the California State Board of Pharmacy (board), sought review of a judgment in administrative mandamus by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which set aside certain penalties imposed upon respondent corporation for false, misleading, and illegal advertising and remanded the case to the board for reconsideration of those penalties.


OVERVIEW: The board suspended the corporation's permits for false, misleading, and illegal advertising. The trial court set aside the penalties stating that they were arbitrary, capricious, an abuse of the board's discretion, and not supported by substantial evidence. On appeal, the court modified and affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that the imposition of lighter penalties on other companies for similar customs and practices had no bearing on whether the corporation violated the law. The court found that, because the board imposed separate penalties for each statutory violation, the corporation's partial exoneration did not compel a remand of the case. The board's penalties could have been held unreasonably severe only if they imposed an unreasonable hardship on the corporation. The court stated that declarations of the corporation's secretary alleging such hardships was not properly introduced into evidence and was inadmissible as hearsay evidence. The court found that witness testimony that the penalties would cost the corporation well over $ 100,000 was unsupported by any computations and fell short of establishing unreasonable hardship to the corporation.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment of the trial court by striking the paragraphs therein setting aside penalties imposed by the state board of pharmacy against the corporation for false, misleading, and illegal advertising. As modified, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

People v. Wade


Crim. No. 12983


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


266 Cal. App. 2d 918; 72 Cal. Rptr. 538; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1585



October 29, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied November 13, 1968, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 24, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Raymond R. Roberts, Judge.

Prosecution for burglary.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction of second degree burglary affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted defendant after a jury trial of burglary of the second degree, denied defendant's motion for anew trial and motion in arrest of judgment, denied his application for probation, and sentenced defendant to an indeterminate prison term. Prior to the trial, defendant admitted the truth of the allegations of the prior convictions of felony.


OVERVIEW: While responding to a silent alarm, a police officer saw defendant coming out of the gate to a school. He was carrying a radio and wore mismatched gloves. A pry bar he tossed into his car matched the indentation on a window frame that looked like the point of entry. Defendant argued in part that he did not make a knowing and intelligent waiver of counsel upon his arraignment; his prior convictions were improperly admitted in evidence; the prosecutor committed prejudicial misconduct; and the indeterminate sentence law was unconstitutional. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court held that the magistrate did not abuse his discretion in denying defendant's motion to have a deputy public defender appointed to sit in an advisory capacity while defendant represented himself at the preliminary hearing. The court found that defendant could not challenge the validity of his prior convictions for the first time on appeal and was not prejudiced by the prosecutor's suggestion that information about the school's security system might fall into the wrong hands. The court concluded that the indeterminate sentence law was not cruel and unusual punishment under the Eighth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for second degree burglary.

 

1149 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Regents of University of Cal. v. Morris


Civ. No. 30694


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


266 Cal. App. 2d 616; 72 Cal. Rptr. 406; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1549



October 18, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied November 13, 1968, and the Petition of the Defendants and Appellants for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 11, 1968. Peters, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from a judgment and final order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Arnold Praeger, Judge.

PROCEEDING in eminent domain to condemn real property for use of a university.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part. Judgment of condemnation reversed solely as to issue of damages.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant landowners sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which entered a monetary judgment in favor of the landowners in an eminent domain proceeding wherein plaintiff university condemned as public grounds the landowners' property.


OVERVIEW: The university condemned as public grounds the landowners' property and initiated an eminent domain proceeding. The trial court entered a monetary judgment in favor of the landowners, and the landowners sought review contending that the trial court erred on the damages issue. The court held that the trial court improperly refused to admit evidence of the probability of rezoning of the property in the near future and held that the jury should have considered such evidence. The court held that pretrial disclosure of the appraisers' opinions was necessary for the parties to fairly evaluate their respective claims. The court held that the landowners who accepted payments of damages awarded to them for the taking of their land were estopped from contesting the validity of the proceedings. However, the court held that prohibition could have issued when it was shown that the trial court erroneously overruled a demurrer. The court reversed a judgment of the trial court solely on the issue of damages and affirmed the remainder of the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment of the trial court solely on the issue of damages and affirmed the remainder of the judgment entered in favor of the landowners in an eminent domain action against the university. Although the landowners were estopped from contesting the validity of the proceedings after accepting payments of damages for the taking of their land, prohibition could have issued when the trial court erroneously overruled a demurrer.

 

1150 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Steely


Crim. No. 6640


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


266 Cal. App. 2d 591; 72 Cal. Rptr. 368; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1546



October 17, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied November 15, 1968, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 11, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Monterey County. Anthony Brazil, Judge.

Prosecution for possession of a sharp instrument while confined in a state prison.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Based upon a jury's finding of guilt, the Superior Court of Monterey County (California) entered a judgment of conviction against defendant, an inmate, for possession of a sharp instrument while confined in a state prison, a violation of Cal. Penal Code § 4502. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A corrections officer broke up an altercation between defendant and another inmate. The corrections officer searched defendant and found an ice pick type of weapon, approximately 10 inches in length, stuffed in defendant's trousers. Subsequently, defendant was convicted of possession of a sharp instrument while confined in a state prison. On review, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction. The court found that under Cal. Penal Code § 4502, proof of knowing possession of a sharp instrument by defendant was sufficient for conviction. The court further held that it was not necessary for the People to establish the intent or purpose for which defendant possessed the instrument. Furthermore, the court rejected defendant's claim that § 4502 was unconstitutionally vague and uncertain. Lastly, the court held that the correctional facility where defendant was housed at the time of the crime was a "state prison," within the meaning of § 4502.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1151 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Billon


Crim. No. 6894


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


266 Cal. App. 2d 537; 72 Cal. Rptr. 198; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1540



October 16, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Napa County. William L. Blanckenburg, Judge.

Prosecution for possession of a firearm by one previously convicted of a felony involving the use of a firearm.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment of conviction reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Napa County (California), which convicted him of possession of a firearm by a person previously convicted of a felony while using a firearm in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 12560.


OVERVIEW: At trial, the prosecution presented a certified copy of defendant's prior conviction of assault with a deadly weapon, but produced no evidence to show that this offense involved the use of a firearm. On appeal, defendant contended that Cal. Penal Code § 12560 was unconstitutional and that there was no evidence at trial to show that his prior conviction involved the use of a firearm. The court rejected defendant's constitutional argument but found merit in the contention that there was a lack of evidence of the use of a firearm. The court found that defendant's use of a firearm in his prior felony conviction was an essential element of the charged offense and unless it was proven, violation of Cal. Penal Code § 12560 was not established. The court noted that although defendant's prior conviction was for assault with a deadly weapon, not all deadly weapons were firearms. The court declined to take judicial notice of the transcript of defendant's preliminary hearing pertaining to the prior felony because the transcript was not offered at trial and to do so would be to deny defendant the right of trial by jury. Thus, the court reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for possession of a firearm by a person previously convicted of a felony while using a firearm.

 

1152 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Maloy v. Municipal Court of Los Angeles Judicial Dist.


Civ. No. 33477


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


266 Cal. App. 2d 414; 72 Cal. Rptr. 207; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1526



October 7, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitioner's Application for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 4, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING in prohibition to prohibit the Municipal Court for the Los Angeles Judicial District of Los Angeles County from prosecuting petitioner for repossessing automobiles without a city permit.



DISPOSITION: Alternative writ discharged; peremptory writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner applicant filed a proceeding in prohibition to prohibit respondent Municipal Court for the Los Angeles Judicial District of Los Angeles County (California) from prosecuting the applicant for repossessing automobiles without a city permit.


OVERVIEW: Though granted a license to repossess cars by the state, the applicant was denied a city license to do so under a city ordinance. The court issued an alternative writ because of the importance of the question involved, which was whether the state had preempted the field of regulatory licensing of repossessors of personalty. The applicant contended that the enactment of Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 460 resulted in preemption the field of regulatory licensing of repossession and that the ordinance, which subjected him to criminal penalties for failure to obtain a permit, was therefore void. The court found that, only where there was a general state law conflicting with a city ordinance was the ordinance unconstitutional. Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 7523.1 was not a delegation of legislative power to local governments to engage in licensing in the area of vehicle repossession and, thus, the state statute specifically prevented preemption of the entire field of law. Thus, the court discharged the alternative writ of prohibition it had instituted and denied the preemptory writ of prohibition.


OUTCOME: The court discharged its alternative writ of prohibition and denied the applicant peremptory writ of prohibition to prevent the municipal court from prosecuting him for repossession of automobiles without a license.

In re Cleaver

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Solano County granting a writ of habeas corpus releasing a prisoner from custody and reinstating him to parole. Raymond J. Sherwin, Judge. OVERVIEW: The prisoner had been convicted of assault with intent to commit murder in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 217 and of assault with a deadly weapon in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 245, with an admitted prior conviction of possession of a narcotic other than marijuana. The prisoner was sentenced to the state prison. Thereafter, the prisoner's release upon an approved parole plan was authorized, and he was released on parole. While he was on parole, however, the prisoner was arrested for assaulting a police officer in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 245. Thereafter, the state cancelled the prisoner's parole, ordered his return to prison, and refixed his term at maximum for violating parole conditions. The trial court granted the prisoner's writ of habeas corpus. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the trial court erred in receiving evidence on the merits of the charges contained in the reports and orders of the state, and in determining that there was no cause under Cal. Penal Code § 3063 for cancelling the prisoner's parole and returning him to prison. The court further held that the state was authorized to refix the prisoner's prison term to the maximum.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that granted the prisoner's writ of habeas corpus and that released the prisoner from custody and reinstated him to parole. The court granted the state's peremptory writs.

Litzmann v. Workers' Comp. Appeals Bd.


Civ. No. 33021


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


266 Cal. App. 2d 203; 71 Cal. Rptr. 731; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1501; 33 Cal. Comp. Cases 584



September 27, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PROCEEDING to review a decision of the Workmen's Compensation Appeals Board denying a claim for benefits.



DISPOSITION: Decision annulled with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee challenged the decision of the Workmen's Compensation Appeals Board (California), which denied his claim for workers' compensation benefits for injuries sustained during the course of his employment.


OVERVIEW: The employee was involved in an altercation with another employee in the employer's break room. The board's referee found that the employee sustained injury to his right shoulder, right upper arm, and left elbow arising out of and occurring in the course of his employment, but that the injury arose out of an altercation in which the employee was the initial physical aggressor. Therefore, the referee ruled that he was not entitled to an award. The employee argued that there was insufficient evidence to support the referee's finding that he was the aggressor. He also argued that his employer condoned the injuries sustained in the course of horseplay. The court found that there was sufficient evidence that the injuries arose out of and in the course of the employee's employment. However, the court annulled the board's decision because it also found that the evidence did not sustain the finding that the employee was the aggressor. There was no evidence that the employee had any willingness or intent to inflict bodily harm on the other employee or that he actually did inflict any bodily harm on him.


OUTCOME: The board's decision that denied the employee worker's compensation benefits was annulled, and the case was remanded to the board for further proceedings.

 

1155 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Mesa


Crim. No. 3363


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


265 Cal. App. 2d 746; 71 Cal. Rptr. 594; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1675



September 16, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 13, 1968. Peters, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Municipal Court of the North Orange County Judicial District of Orange County granting a new trial in a prosecution for public solicitation of lewd or dissolute conduct. Max V. Eliason, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the order granting a new trial to defendant who was convicted of soliciting another to engage in lewd or dissolute conduct in a public place in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 647(a). The order granting the new trial was issued by the Municipal Court of the North Orange County Judicial District of Orange County (California).


OVERVIEW: Defendant made homosexual advances to an undercover police officer in a bar that suggested to the police officer that defendant wished to have homosexual relations in a private place. The lower court convicted defendant of a violation § 647(a), but it ordered a new trial following the conviction. The court reversed the lower court's order granting a new trial. The court held that penal statutes were to interpreted with a view to the objects of the legislature and to promote justice. The court ruled that the conduct which defendant engaged in would outrage the vast majority of people, and construing § 647(a) in such a way that it prohibited homosexual solicitations in a public place even if the solicited conduct were to take place in a private place was consistent with the legislature's intent. Therefore, the evidence presented was sufficient to convict defendant of a violation of § 647(a).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's order, which granted defendant a new trial following his conviction for soliciting another to engage in lewd or dissolute conduct in a public place.

 

1156 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bammes


Crim. No. 4732


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


265 Cal. App. 2d 626; 71 Cal. Rptr. 415; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1657



September 11, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 7, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Shasta County. Richard W. Abbe, Judge.

Prosecution for failure to stop after an automobile accident.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Shasta County (California) that convicted her after a jury trial of violation of Cal. Veh. Code § 20001, failure by a driver of a vehicle involved in an accident to stop. Defendant's motion to set aside the conviction was denied.


OVERVIEW: Defendant turned her car into an intersection in front of an oncoming station wagon, which collided with a logging truck killing five occupants of the station wagon. On appeal from her conviction under Cal. Veh. Code § 20001, defendant conceded that there need not necessarily be some contact between defendant's vehicle and that of another for a defendant to be involved in an accident under § 20001. The court rejected defendant's contentions that her actions had not caused or contributed to the accident and that if they did she was unaware of that fact. The evidence at trial established that her action in turning into the intersection in front of the station wagon was an efficient cause of the latter's colliding with the truck and that therefore defendant was involved in the accident. The court ruled that compliance with § 20001 did not require defendant to confess responsibility for the accident or to be a witness against herself. The court also held that the statute was not void for vagueness. The conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment which convicted defendant of failure by a driver of a vehicle involved in an accident to stop.

 

1157 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Rivera v. Division of Industrial Welfare


Civ. No. 12023


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


265 Cal. App. 2d 576; 71 Cal. Rptr. 739; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1653; 1 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P9876



September 10, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitions for a Rehearing were Denied October 9, 1968, and the Petitions of the Real Parties in Interest for a Hearing by the Supreme Court were Denied October 31, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING in mandamus to compel the Department of Industrial Relations and the Division of Industrial Welfare to enforce certain orders regulating wages, hours and working conditions of women and minors in agricultural and allied pursuits and to compel vacation of orders restraining enforcement issued by the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco and the Superior Court of Los Angeles County.



DISPOSITION: Writ granted; alternative writs discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner agricultural workers sought a mandamus action to compel respondent enforcement agencies to enforce orders regulating minimum wages, maximum hours and working conditions of petitioners, and to compel vacation of partial restraints against enforcement, which had been issued by the superior courts of San Francisco and Los Angeles.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner agricultural workers sought an action to compel enforcement of orders adopted by the Industrial Welfare Commission (Commission) establishing wages and hours for women and minors in agricultural industries. The order had been stayed pending outcome of other actions brought by relator employers. The court found the orders valid, ordered enforcement by respondent enforcement agencies, and ordered the superior courts to vacate their stays. The Commission's quasi-legislative role exempted it from stringent constitutional due process requirements, such as cross-examination of public hearing witnesses. The Commission's determination was judgmental as well as factual, so that it could rely on witness opinion without the oath requirement. Relators had access to the hearings and underlying studies upon which the orders were adopted. The minimum wage was appropriate based on a statutory provision implying discretion, and a policy that the rate be "not less than" adequate. Overtime rates harmonized with provisions of the Fair Labor Standards Act and legislative intent. Federal statutes did not preempt the orders in the absence of case law or legislative intent to the contrary.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioner agricultural workers' request that respondent enforcement agencies enforce the wage and hour orders, and ordered the superior courts to vacate their stays. The Industrial Welfare Commission did not have to put public hearing witnesses under oath. There was a statutory basis for the wage order, the overtime rates harmonized with the Fair Labor Standards Act, and federal statutes did not preempt the orders.

Arenstein v. California State Bd. of Pharmacy

Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the Superior Court of Los Angeles County to reconsider a judgment upholding a decision of the State Board of Phramacy that certain pharmacy licenses should be suspended.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ and discharging alternative writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, pharmacists and corporation employing them, challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which upheld a decision of respondent state board of pharmacy finding that appellants' licenses were to be suspended.


OVERVIEW: Respondent state board of pharmacy filed an administrative accusation charging appellant pharmacists with refilling prescriptions for dangerous drugs without authorization of the prescribers, and charging that appellant corporation employing them was subject to discipline because of the acts. Respondent adopted the hearing officer's proposed decision suspending the pharmacy permit of appellant corporation and the professional licenses of appellant pharmacists, and appellants petitioned for a writ of mandate. The lower court denied the petition, and appellants sought review. The court held that the record supported the lower court's determination upholding respondent's findings that appellant pharmacists refilled prescriptions for dangerous drugs without authorization from prescribers and that such acts authorized suspension of their licenses. The court held that evidence of the illegal acts of appellant pharmacists supported disciplining appellant corporation. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the evidence supported the lower court's determination upholding respondent state board of pharmacy's findings that the illegal acts of appellant pharmacists in refilling prescriptions for dangerous drugs without authorization from prescribers warranted the suspension of the licenses of appellants, pharmacists and corporation employing them.

Burns v. State Compensation Ins. Fund


Civ. No. 23841


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


265 Cal. App. 2d 98; 71 Cal. Rptr. 326; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1604; 33 Cal. Comp. Cases 931



August 22, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 17, 1968. Peters, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgments of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Joseph Karesh, Judge.

Action for damages for personal injuries allegedly resulting from negligent inspection of unsafe conditions at a sawmill.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal as to one defendant after demurrer to first amended complaint was sustained without leave to amend affirmed, and summary judgment as to other defendant affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimant challenged the decision of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which sustained the demurrer to his complaint for personal injury damages against defendant state compensation insurance fund, and granted summary judgment in favor of defendant state inspection rating bureau.


OVERVIEW: The claimant contended that the fund and the bureau's failure to properly inspect a sawmill caused the amputation of the claimant's leg in a workplace accident. The court affirmed the trial court's decision to grant summary judgment in favor of the bureau because the bureau enjoyed immunity under Cal. Ins. Code § 11758. The court affirmed the trial court's decision to sustain the demurrer of the fund because the fund also enjoyed immunity under the doctrine of stare decisis. The court rejected claimant's contention that he was denied equal protection because the court found the legislative scheme authorizing worksite inspections was a reasonable classification for the purpose of improving workplace safety, and that absent immunity, there was no incentive for such inspections to occur.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to sustain the fund's demurrer to the claimant's personal injury complaint, and to grant summary judgment in favor of the bureau.

 

1160 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Holden v. Arnebergh


Civ. Nos. 32155, 32197


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


265 Cal. App. 2d 87; 71 Cal. Rptr. 401; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1602



August 21, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied September 3, 1968, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 17, 1968. Peters, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from orders of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County dismissing two actions for declaratory relief and denying a motion to strike a cost bill of the several defendants. Richard L. Wells and Robert H. Thompson, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant store owners sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which dismissed their two actions for declaratory relief and denied a motion to strike a cost bill of appellees, city and police officers.


OVERVIEW: The owners were arrested and charged with violating Cal. Penal Code § 311.2, exhibiting and selling obscene material. They sought a declaratory judgment that the statute deprived them of rights guaranteed by the First, Fourth, and 14th Amendments of the U.S. Constitution, that the materials seized were not obscene and not the subject of criminal prosecution. The owners sought injunctive relief against further prosecution for selling and exhibiting such materials. The trial court sustained appellees' demurrers and the owners sought review under Cal. Code Civ. Proc. § 581(3). They also appealed the order denying their motion to strike cost bill of appellees pursuant to Cal. Gov. Code § 951(b). On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that that there was substance to neither contention of the store owners. The court held that it was immaterial whether the property was illegally seized by means of an invalid warrant or without any warrant at all. The court found that the store owners did not make any showing that the present proceeding should have been considered an exception to the general rule that the granting of relief rests in the sound discretion of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders of the trial court.

 

1161 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


L. B. Foster Co. v. County of Los Angeles


Civ. No. 31596


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


265 Cal. App. 2d 24; 71 Cal. Rptr. 16; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1593



August 19, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 17, 1968. Mosk, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Carlos M. Teran, Judge.

Action for refund of property taxes paid under protest pursuant to escaped and penal assessments.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Summary judgment for plaintiff reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer instituted an action against defendants, county and assessor, in order to receive a refund of property taxes that it paid under protest. The Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) granted the taxpayer's motion for summary judgment as to an amount which represented penalties that the taxpayer paid pursuant to Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code §§ 503, 504. The county and the assessor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer paid property taxes under protest pursuant to combined escaped and penal assessments that were made by the assessor under Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code §§ 503, 504. The taxpayer instituted an action by which it sought a refund. The taxpayer filed a motion for summary judgment. The superior court granted summary judgment for an amount that represented the portion of the taxes that arose from the penal assessments on the ground that §§ 501, 503, and 504 were unconstitutional. The county and the assessor appealed. Upon review, the court reversed the judgment. The court held that the delegation of power to the assessor did not implicate separation of power issues because he was a county officer, and strict separation of powers did not exist in county government, nor was it constitutionally required. The court held that the penalties did not violate the state constitutional requirements regarding the uniformity or proportionality of property taxation; the penalty was a civil sanction over and above the collection of the tax which resulted from uniform assessment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment to the taxpayer in its action against the county and the assessor in which it sought to obtain a refund of property taxes that it paid under protest.

 

1162 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


De Jong v. Pasadena Unified School Dist.


Civ. No. 33240


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


264 Cal. App. 2d 877; 70 Cal. Rptr. 913; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2157



August 12, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied August 30, 1968, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 9, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Charles A. Loring, Judge.

Action to test the validity of bonds issued pursuant to a school bond election.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed on motion. Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted defendant school district' motion for summary judgment in the taxpayer's action to test the validity of bonds issued pursuant to a school bond election.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer brought an action that challenged the validity of bonds issued against the school district who were granted authority to conduct and certify the regularity of election proceedings under Cal. Educ. Code § 21708. The school district brought a motion for summary judgment that was granted by the trial court. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court called the taxpayer's appeal frivolous because he failed to argue that he had a vested right in the results of the first counting of ballots and that the later recount pursuant to Cal. Educ. Code § 1443 had unconstitutionally deprived him of this right. The court held that a validating statute with respect to the bonds of public bodies enacted by the legislature that included school district's within its scope was dispositive in the case. The court held that such a curative statute served to validate all defects in an election proceeding with the exception of those that resulted in constitutional rights violations. The court held that mere irregularities of procedure in the election were not constitutional rights violations and the bonds issued were valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of the school district's motion for summary judgment in the taxpayer's action to challenge the validity of bonds issued in a school bond election.

 

1163 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Irvin


Crim. No. 6691


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


264 Cal. App. 2d 747; 70 Cal. Rptr. 892; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2142



August 7, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 3, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Mateo County and from an order granting probation as to one defendant. Louis D. DeMatteis, Judge.

Prosecution for burglary and for the illegal possession of marijuana as to one defendant.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of convictions affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed their convictions after a jury trial from the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California) for burglary of the first degree in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 459. One defendant was further found guilty of possession of marijuana in violation of Cal. Health and Safety Code § 11530.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were observed by a victim, who did not see their faces, but testified to the characteristics of the two men who fled his apartment. A police officer stopped defendants based on their description, and one of them picked up a stolen purse from the street. Defendants jointly contended that they were illegally stopped and that the fruits of the arrest were erroneously admitted, that evidence of the victim's identification of defendants was erroneously admitted, or in any event, admitted without a finding by the court that the procedure was fair and reasonable. The court held that no question of illegal arrest, search, or seizure was raised in the trial court and the issue could not be raised for the first time on appeal. Furthermore, the evidence failed to disclose any search. It was also clear that there was no unfairness in the identification procedure. The totality of the circumstances had to be viewed in the light of the identification that resulted. The victim at no time attempted to unqualifiedly identify either defendant as one of the persons who was in his driveway. This identification did not diverge from rudimentary fairness. The convictions were affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendants' convictions for burglary and possession of marijuana were affirmed.

People v. Greene


Crim. No. 14879


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


264 Cal. App. 2d 774; 70 Cal. Rptr. 818; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2144



August 7, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 3, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Municipal Court of the Los Angeles Judicial District of Los Angeles County. James Harvey Brown, Judge.

Prosecution for misdemeanor violation of failing to correct an existing excavation and fill determined to be a dangerous condition.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Municipal Court of the Los Angeles Judicial District of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted him of a misdemeanor violation of failing to correct an existing excavation and fill determined to be a dangerous condition, in violation of Los Angeles, Cal., Municipal Code § 91.0103(n).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of a misdemeanor for failing to correct an existing excavation and fill determined to be a dangerous condition, in violation of Los Angeles, Cal., Municipal Code § 91.0103(n). The appellate department of the superior court reversed the conviction, declaring the ordinance unconstitutional. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that the ordinance was not unconstitutional. The court held that the ordinance was basically a nuisance ordinance, and it was appropriate for such an ordinance to be directed against dangerous conditions without regard for the cause of the condition. The court also held that it was not unconstitutional that the ordinance required correction of a condition that is dangerous to persons, property, and the public highway. The court further held that defendant's objection to the ordinance as possibly subjecting a landowner to unlimited expense was irrelevant because defendant was challenging the constitutionality of the ordinance on its face only.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

 

1165 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Phillis v. Santa Barbara


Civ. No. 31560


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


264 Cal. App. 2d 781; 70 Cal. Rptr. 573; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2145



August 7, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALS from a judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Barbara County. Edward L. Brady, Judge. *


* Assigned by the Chairman of the Judicial Council.

Action by former employees to recover retirement benefits allegedly due, and to recover salary deductions allegedly due one plaintiff.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment establishing right to pensions and denying right to retroactive accruals and deductions from salary, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, former fireman and former policeman, and defendant city appealed a decision of the Superior Court of Santa Barbara County (California), which held that the former employees were entitled to receive pensions, to recover installments which had accrued within the three-year period of limitations prescribed in Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 338 (1), and that they were not entitled to recover installments which had accrued earlier.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed an action against the city to recover retirement benefits. The policeman sought a return of the money deducted from his salary for the pension fund. The trial court dismissed plaintiffs action, and the appellate court reversed. On remand, the trial court held that plaintiffs were entitled to receive pensions; that each was entitled to recover installments which had accrued within the three-year period of limitations prescribed in Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 338(1); that neither was entitled to recover installments which had accrued earlier; and that the policeman's claim for money deducted from his salary was entirely barred by the statute of limitations. Both parties appealed, and the court affirmed. The court concluded that the city's attorney failed to realize that the policeman was already entitled to retirement status under a previous charter, but that his good faith mistake did not estop the city from asserting the statute of limitations with respect to the salary deductions. The court concluded that the policeman attained the status of a retired member entitled to receive a pension.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment establishing plaintiffs' right to pensions and denying a right to retroactive accruals and deductions from their salary in their action against the city.

 

1166 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kagan


Crim. No. 6378


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


264 Cal. App. 2d 648; 70 Cal. Rptr. 732; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2129



August 5, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied August 28, 1968, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 3, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Francis McCarty, Judge.

Prosecution for grand theft and forgery.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which convicted him of grand theft, Cal. Penal Code § 487, and forgery, Cal. Penal Code § 470.


OVERVIEW: The court rejected defendant's contention that a photocopy of an altered photocopy could not be a forged instrument. The court found that defendant forged the original photocopy of a letter of credit with intent to defraud the complainant, who acted upon it as genuine. The court found that the complainant gave the money to defendant for a particular purpose, to buy letters of credit, and that he never intended to do so but instead transferred most of the money into his personal accounts. The court found that such evidence sufficed to constitute larceny by trick. Furthermore, the court found that defendant took these funds impressed with a trust, so he was guilty of embezzlement. The court found that there was an implied promise by defendant that he would return any unutilized funds from the letters of credit and that the complainant parted with her money on the basis of the representation that she would get her money back if the funds were not utilized. The court concluded that the elements of the crime of false pretenses were made out.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1167 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Rowland School Dist. v. State Board of Education


Civ. No. 31610


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


264 Cal. App. 2d 589; 70 Cal. Rptr. 504; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2121



August 1, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALS from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Ralph H. Nutter, Judge.

Action for declaratory relief and for an injunction to prevent the State Board of Education from holding an election for the purpose of unifying certain school districts.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal after demurrers to second amended complaint were sustained without leave to amend affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff school districts appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied the school districts' request for declaratory relief and to enjoin defendant California State Board of Education from holding an election in order to vote on unifying the school districts.


OVERVIEW: The board held an election for the purpose of unifying the school districts during which most of the voters voted "no." The school districts were opposed to unification so in anticipation of the next election, which would be held within two years, the school districts filed an action for declaratory relief and an injunction to prevent the board from taking further steps toward unification. The school districts contended that certain sections of the Cal. Educ. Code were unconstitutional. The trial court denied the school districts' requests for declaratory relief and an injunction. The school districts appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed, ruling that the school districts were seeking relief concerning an action that was merely anticipated or being considered in the future. Thus, their complaint did not plead a present cause of action or establish an imminent situation, which would justify declaratory relief or an injunction, and the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying declaratory relief to the school districts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the school districts' action seeking declaratory relief and an injunction to prevent the board from taking further action to unify the school districts.

People v. Oatis


Crim. No. 14009


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


264 Cal. App. 2d 324; 70 Cal. Rptr. 524; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2089



July 25, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 3, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Kathleen Parker, Judge.

Prosecution for the possession of marijuana and the sale of marijuana.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) convicted defendant of possession of marijuana and the sale of marijuana. The trial court denied defendant's motion for a new trial. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Two of defendant's acquaintances brought an undercover police officer to defendant for purchases of marijuana. When the officer was first introduced to defendant, defendant was standing at a kitchen counter in front of a bulk amount of marijuana. Defendant made two sales of marijuana to the undercover officer. Defendant alleged that he was entrapped by the undercover officer, that the prohibition of possession of marijuana as a crime was unconstitutional and that the evidence was insufficient to support the judgment. The court held that, as a matter of law, there was no entrapment and that the defense could not be raised for the first time on appeal. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction. Defendant sold the undercover agent a half pound of marijuana from the bulk that was on the counter. The circumstances did not substantiate an entrapment defense. The court held that the criminalization of marijuana was constitutional. The legislature had a rational, public purpose in criminializing the possession of marijuana.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1169 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Fallis v. Department of Motor Vehicles


Civ. No. 8835


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


264 Cal. App. 2d 373; 70 Cal. Rptr. 595; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2094



July 25, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. Edgar B. Hervey, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to command the Department of Motor Vehicles to set aside an order suspending a driver's license.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment granting peremptory writ reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff licensee brought a proceeding in mandamus to compel defendant Department of Motor Vehicles to set aside an order suspending his driver's license under Cal. Veh. Code § 13353. The Superior Court of San Diego County (California) issued the requested writ, and the department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The licensee was stopped, read his rights, and asked if he would consent to a blood alcohol test. The licensee requested an attorney and stated that he would not take a test without his doctor and witnesses. At an informal hearing requested by the licensee, the referee recommended suspension of his driver's license under § 13353. The trial court set aside the suspension based on a finding that the licensee was not obliged to make a statement to the officer after having requested and been denied counsel. Thus, the trial court found no refusal to take the test. The court reversed the trial court's judgment, finding that the Fifth and First Amendments did not protect the licensee in refusing to submit to a test under § 13353. Further, the licensee could not qualify his consent on the condition that the test be administered by his physician. The right to counsel did not apply to the consent or refusal to submit to a test under § 13353. On remand, the trial court was to consider the sufficiency of the evidence before the referee because the sworn statement of the officer that there was reasonable cause for the stop was not alone sufficient to overcome evidence to the contrary.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's peremptory writ requiring the department to set aside the suspension of the licensee's driver's license and remanded for a determination of the sufficiency of the evidence before the department's referee.

Hillman v. Stults

July 12, 1968

Consolidated actions to determine title to real and personal property, impress a trust and require an accounting of the handling of said property, compel a conveyance and transfer and to establish any outstanding leases and declare the rights and duties of litigants as to future rental payments on said leases.

OVERVIEW: The court consolidated appeals from certain orders involving a conservatorship and a receivership and a judgment holding that extensive ranch holdings, real and personal property of the former prisoner that were held in trust for him by his sister. The sister was dead, and the estate was substituted through her husband who was the defendant as administrator and an individual. Serenko v. Bright


Civ. No. 31848


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


263 Cal. App. 2d 682; 70 Cal. Rptr. 1; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2257



July 8, 1968

Proceeding in mandamus and prohibition to restrain the Department of Motor Vehicles from suspending plaintiff's driving license.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writs affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver challenged an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied her application for a writ of mandamus and prohibition against respondent Department of Motor Vehicles taking her license under Cal. Veh. Code § 13353.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied the application for a writ of mandamus and prohibition that the driver filed as to the Department of Motor Vehicles taking her license under § 13353 because she refused to submit to a blood alcohol test when she was arrested for driving while intoxicated. The court affirmed that denial on appeal. The court reasoned that § 13353 did not unconstitutionally abridge the privileges that were associated with a driver's license because driving gave rise to an implied consent to take a chemical test. The court also held that there was substantial and uncontroverted evidence that the driver refused to take the chemical test. The court further concluded that the record showed that the formal hearing that the driver contained all the required elements of rudimentary fairness and the added protection of adequate judicial review and that her due process rights were not violated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a denial of the writ of mandamus and prohibition for which the driver applied as to the Department of Motor Vehicles taking her license after she refused to take a blood alcohol test in conjunction with her arrest for driving while intoxicated.

Datil v. City of Los Angeles


Civ. No. 31745


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


263 Cal. App. 2d 655; 69 Cal. Rptr. 788; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2253



July 2, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition of a Rehearing was Denied July 18, 1968, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied August 28, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Robert H. Patton, Judge.

Action against a city for wrongful death of person under arrest killed by fellow arrestee.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendant affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff arrestee's widow sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which concluded that a wrongful death action brought against defendant city was barred by Cal. Gov't Code §§ 844.6, 845.2. The arrestee's widow brought the action after the arrestee died from injuries received during a jail fight.


OVERVIEW: The arrestee, who had been punched during a jail fight, died from a fractured skull. Thereafter, the arrestee's widow brought a wrongful death action against the city, claiming the city police department had been negligent and careless in supervising the inmates and prisoners of the jail. After the trial court held the action was barred by Cal. Gov't Code §§ 844.6, 845.2, the arrestee's widow sought review, and the court affirmed. In affirming that Cal. Gov't Code §§ 844.6, 845.2 had protected the city from liability for prisoner injuries, the court held the arrestee had been a prisoner under Cal. Gov't Code § 844 because the arrestee had been booked, as provided in Cal. Penal Code § 7(21). The court also stated the test for determining if an arrestee was a prisoner was not whether the arrestee had been informed against, indicted, arraigned, tried, or convicted. Finally, the court rejected an argument that the California Tort Claims Act of 1963, of which Cal. Gov't Code §§ 844.6, 845.2 were a part, was unconstitutional because the state had delegated its own immunity to subordinates entities, such as the city.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that concluded a wrongful death action brought by the arrestee's widow against the city was barred.

Hargens v. Alcoholic Beverage Control Appeals Board


Civ. No. 32796


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


263 Cal. App. 2d 601; 69 Cal. Rptr. 868; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2245



June 28, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied July 12, 1968, and Petitioners' Application for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied August 21, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING to review a decision of the Alcoholic Beverage Control Appeals Board affirming a department decision suspending an on-sale beer and wine license.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner licensees challenged a judgment of respondent California Alcoholic Beverage Control Appeals Board, which affirmed a decision of the real party in interest, the California Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control, that suspended the licensees' on-sale beer and wine license under Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 23090 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The licensees were accused of using the services of a female person, who was not the wife of a licensee, in the dispensing of wine from behind a permanently affixed fixture that was used to prepare alcoholic beverages on the licensed premises in violation of Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 25656. After a hearing, the Department's hearing officer recommended suspension of the licensees' license for five days. Such decision was adopted by the Department and affirmed by the Board. The licensees argued that § 25656 was unconstitutional because it violated U.S. Const. amends. V and XIV and because it denied them equal protection of the laws. The licensees also argued that it violated their rights under Cal. Const. art. XX, § 18. The court disagreed with the licensees and held that § 25656 was constitutional. Specifically, the court found that the enactment of § 25656 was a proper exercise of the police power of the State of California and noted that § 25656 did not abridge the privileges and immunities of or deny equal protection of the laws to the licensees as employers, any more than it abridged the constitutional rights of the woman who was their employee.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1174 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Walberg


Crim. No. 13657


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


263 Cal. App. 2d 286; 69 Cal. Rptr. 457; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2207



June 19, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALS from judgments (orders granting probation) of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Aubrey N. Irwin, Judge.

Prosecutions for selling securities without a permit of the Commissioner of Corporations.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgments of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) granting defendants probation based upon jury finding defendants guilty of selling securities without a permit from the Commissioner of Corporations, in violation of Cal. Corp. Code § 26104(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendants solicited loans for a ministry project of refurbishing an old hotel. Defendants printed and distributed literature offering to pay 6 percent interest on the loans. No permit to issue securities had been obtained from Commissioner of Corporations. Defendants were convicted and sentenced to probation for selling securities without a permit in violation of Cal. Corp. Code § 26104(a). Defendants appealed. Defendants argued that the promissory notes were not securities. Court disagreed. Court held that the notes issued here clearly fell within the statutory definition of a security since the notes were sold in order to obtain borrowed working capital. Revisions to the statute had made it clear that a note could be a security even though it did not give the holder a proprietary interest or share of profits. Court found no error with the jury instructions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' probation and conviction, holding that defendants' conduct of selling promissory notes that were advertised and indiscriminately offered to the public at large fell well within the literal reading of the California Corporate Securities Act.
