Widdows v. Koch


Civ. No. 8917


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


263 Cal. App. 2d 228; 69 Cal. Rptr. 464; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2528; 1968 Trade Cas. (CCH) P72,518



June 18, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Bernardino County. Joseph T. Ciano, Judge.

Action by a private ambulance owner against a municipality and its officials for damages and declaratory relief for conspiracy to restrain trade.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal after demurrer sustained without leave to amend affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, ambulance service provider, challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of San Bernardino County (California), which held that respondents, city government and its employees, were not liable for antitrust violations, after respondents enacted a directive that the city's hospital was to use a competitor's ambulance service unless not practicable.


OVERVIEW: Appellant provided ambulatory services to respondent city and its employees. After a requested subsidiary from respondent was denied, appellant threatened to discontinue service. Respondent filed a motion to expand competition within the city, and enacted a directive that the city's hospital would hereafter use a competitor's ambulance over appellant, unless it was not practicable. Appellant sued respondents for antitrust violations. The court held that while antitrust laws did not apply to city governments, they did apply to its employees. The court also determined that all the employees enjoyed immunity for respondent city's discretionary acts in giving a preference to appellant's competitor, and subsequently affirmed the dismissal of the suit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1176 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lipscomb


Crim. No. 13411


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


263 Cal. App. 2d 59; 69 Cal. Rptr. 127; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2180



June 13, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied August 8, 1968. Peters, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County committing defendant to the Director of Corrections for narcotic treatment. Robert Clifton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant arrestee sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which committed him to respondent state for narcotic treatment.


OVERVIEW: The arrestee appeared to be under the influence of a narcotic and showed external evidence of longtime hypodermic usage, was arrested, advised of his rights, and taken to the police station. In the jail infirmary, he was examined by a staff physician who declared that he was addicted to narcotics or in imminent danger of becoming addicted. A petition for the arrestee's commitment was filed under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 3100.3. The trial court committed the arrestee to the state for narcotic treatment. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that once it was accepted that it was a civil proceeding and once the examining physicians brought to the court essential information without which the court could not act, there was no compelling reason to cut down the scope of that information by requiring a physician to advise a person under examination that he need not talk for fear of incrimination. The arrestee was advised of his rights at the time of arrest and again at the police station. A warning by the examining physician was not required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which committed the arrestee to the state for narcotic treatment.

 

1177 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Coleman v. Silverberg Plumbing Co.


Civ. No. 30991


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


263 Cal. App. 2d 74; 69 Cal. Rptr. 158; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2182; 33 Cal. Comp. Cases 906



June 13, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied July 5, 1968, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied August 8, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Parks Stillwell, Judge.

Action for wrongful death.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of nonsuit affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff survivors appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted a nonsuit to defendant contractor.


OVERVIEW: The decedent of the survivors was killed while working for a subcontractor who did not have workers' compensation insurance. The survivors brought a wrongful death action against the contractor, but counsel for the survivors admitted that the contractor had workers' compensation insurance. The lower court granted a nonsuit to the contractor, and the court affirmed. The court held that the survivors did not have a claim for the wrongful death of a presumptive employee caused by the contractor's presumptive negligence, because Cal. Lab. Code § 3708 only permitted such actions when the alleged employer did not have workers' compensation insurance. The court rejected the survivor's alternative claim for strict liability because the decedent was an employee of the independent subcontractor, and general contractors were not liable for injuries suffered by the employees of independent contractors. The court also ruled that the survivors had no nuisance claim under Cal. Lab. Code § 3712 because § 3712 only applied in the employer and employee context.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court which granted a nonsuit to the contractor.

 

1178 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Salcido


Crim. No. 396


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


263 Cal. App. 2d 1; 69 Cal. Rptr. 193; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2174



June 11, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied July 10, 1968, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied August 8, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Merced County. Donald R. Fretz, Judge.

Prosecution for murder.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction of second degree murder affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of conviction entered by the Superior Court of Merced County (California), which found defendant guilty of murder in the second degree in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 1382, upon a retrial after defendant's successful appeal to the court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and the victim, his girlfriend were in the backseat of a car. The were arguing about defendant's relationships with other women and their own relationship. Defendant threatened to kill the victim several times and finally shot her in the chest. Defendant contended that failure to bring him to trial within the 60-day period as provided for in Cal. Penal Code § 1382(2) violated his rights to a speedy trial. The court disagreed. The court found that whether a delay in completing a persecution amounted to an unconstitutional deprivation of rights depended upon the circumstances. The 24-day delay was not prejudicial to defendant where it was not purposeful or oppressive, was the result of the unavailability of witnesses, was for good cause, and did not affect the outcome of the proceeding. In addition, where defendant failed to discharge his duty of going forward with evidence of mitigating circumstances to the point of raising a reasonable doubt in the minds of the jurors, the presumption of malice operated and the homicide was deemed malicious and an act of murder. Without mitigating evidence there was no reason to reduce defendant's conviction to manslaughter.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1179 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Allstate Ins. Co. v. Orlando


Civ. No. 31276


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


262 Cal. App. 2d 858; 69 Cal. Rptr. 702; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2377



June 11, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a Rehearing was Denied July 9, 1968, and the Opinion was Modified to Read as Printed Above. Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied August 8, 1968. Peters, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Brodie Ahlport, Judge.

Action in declaratory relief to determine the right to recover damages under the uninsured motorist clause of an insurance policy.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiff insurance company affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant insured appealed from judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) denying her the right to recover damages from plaintiff insurer under the uninsured motorist clause of an insurance policy.


OVERVIEW: The insurer filed an action against the insured seeking a declaration that she had no right to recover damages under an uninsured motorist clause because she had failed to file a demand for arbitration within one year from the date of her accident as required by Cal. Ins. Code § 11580.2(h). The insurance policy was issued prior to the effective date of the statute. An arbitrator determined that the insured was not barred by limitations from recovering and awarded her damages. The trial court vacated the award on the ground that the arbitrator exceeded his power in deciding the limitations issue. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment in favor of the insurer and held that § 11580.2 did apply to accidents occurring prior to the statute's effective date. The court held that the insured should have either filed suit or demanded arbitration within one year after the statute's effective date. The court also found that the insured's untimeliness meant that the arbitrator did not have jurisdiction to arbitrate and, that therefore, the arbitration proceeding did not preclude the trial court from deciding all issues.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment for the insurer, which dismissed the insured's claim for damages under an uninsured motorist provision of an insurance policy.

 

1180 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Spaniel


Crim. No. 4542


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


262 Cal. App. 2d 878; 69 Cal. Rptr. 202; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2379



June 11, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied July 10, 1968, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied August 8, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Albert H. Mundt, Judge.

Prosecution for kidnaping for the purpose of robbery and for robbery.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which convicted and sentenced him on charges of kidnapping for the purpose of robbery and of robbery by force and violence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced for kidnapping for the purpose of robbery and of robbery by force and violence. Defendant appealed his conviction and the court affirmed. The court held that the fact that defendant did not keep possession of the stolen car did not change the nature of the kidnapping for the purpose of robbery crime. The court also held that defendant was entitled to an instruction that he was relying upon the defense of diminished capacity, and the instruction was given. The court held that the trial court was within its right to refuse defendant's proposed instruction which had been covered by other instructions already given. The court also held that there was no error in excluding jurors opposed to the death penalty if their opinions precluded finding the defendant guilty. Additionally, the record failed to disclose any instance of incompetency of defense counsel. The court held that there was nothing to substantiate defendant's claim that he would not have talked had he known that he would be charged with kidnapping, and the defendant made no contention of lack of mental capacity to stand trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for kidnapping for the purpose of robbery and of robbery by force and violence.

 

1181 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Chavez


Crim. No. 3037


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


262 Cal. App. 2d 422; 68 Cal. Rptr. 759; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2328



May 23, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Bernardino County. James E. Cunningham, Sr., Judge.

Prosecution for kidnaping.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of kidnapping in the Superior Court of San Bernardino County (California) and was sentenced to prison. He appealed his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged several issues on appeal, including: misconduct of the district attorney by calling defendant's wife as a witness, improper examination of a witness, and improper cross-examination; waiver of his right to jury trial by the court's ruling on voluntary nature of defendant's statements; the trial court's failure to instruct that corpus delicti had to be established independent of the extrajudicial statements of defendant; and that the defendant's attorney was incompetent. The court held that: (1) defendant's objection to the wife being called as a witness did not have legislative sanction, there was no authority that bringing a witness into court in prison garb was prejudicial, and the showing of a conviction of a prior felony was proper in impeaching one's own witness; (2) defendant was not in custody when he made a damaging admission and the admission was made after proper Miranda advisement; (3) the corpus delicti was established by an abundance of evidence independent of the defendant's admissions; and (4) defendant's counsel's failure to object to leading questions did not indicate incompetency.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1182 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Department of Public Works v. Investors Diversified Services, Inc.


Civ. No. 31207


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


262 Cal. App. 2d 367; 68 Cal. Rptr. 663; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2321



May 22, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied June 19, 1968, and Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied July 17, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. William E. MacFaden, Judge, and Benjamin J. Ostrin, Court Commissioner, Judge pro tem.

Proceeding in eminent domain to acquire land for the widening of a street.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment awarding defendant allegedly excessive damages reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an eminent domain action, plaintiff Department of Public Works (department) appealed the order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which held that the department could not introduce evidence that if defendant landowner's property was rezoned, the landowner would have to surrender the strip of land which the department sought to take in its eminent domain action.


OVERVIEW: The department sought a 10-foot strip of land from the landowner to widen a street. The city in which the property was located had a policy requiring landowners to dedicate strips of land for the widening of roads if the property of landowners was rezoned to the more valuable residential classification, and the department desired to introduce evidence to that effect. The lower court ruled that the department was foreclosed from introducing evidence that the city would take the strip if the property was rezoned and, based upon a stipulation of the parties as to the value of the land if the possibility of forced dedication was not considered, entered judgment and awarded damages to the landowner. The court reversed, holding that if the landowner wished to introduce evidence about the higher value of his land upon its rezoning to a residential classification, the city had the right to introduce evidence that the landowner would be forced to dedicate the disputed strip. The court ruled that the city under its police powers had the right to require the dedication of the 10-foot strip if the land was rezoned to a residential classification.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment which had held that the department could not introduce evidence that the landowner's 10-foot strip of property would be taken by the city if the landowner's property was rezoned to a residential classification.

 

1183 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Los Angeles v. Standard Oil Co.


Civ. No. 30751


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


262 Cal. App. 2d 118; 68 Cal. Rptr. 512; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2292



May 13, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Petitions for a Rehearing were Denied June 11, 1968, and Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied July 10, 1968. Mosk, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Leon T. David, Judge.

Action for declaratory relief to determine that a statute relating to contribution among tortfeasors responsible for the Baldwin Hills Reservoir disaster is constitutional.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment for defendant after its demurrer was sustained reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which sustained the demurrer of respondent oil company on the ground that the statute enacted by the legislature relating to contribution among tortfeasors responsible for the Baldwin Hill Reservoir disaster was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The city filed an appeal to the lower court's order sustaining the demurrer of the oil company on the ground that the statute enacted by the legislature relating to contribution among tortfeasors responsible for the Baldwin Hill Reservoir disaster was unconstitutional. The lower court held that the statute was special legislation based upon an invalid classification. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the statute did not violate the constitutional guarantees against special and arbitrary legislation because it provided for a different right of contribution among tortfeasors who may be liable for injuries caused by the disaster from that applicable to tortfeasors in general. The court held that good grounds existed for the distinction made between the parties responsible for the Baldwin Hills damage and tortfeasors who may have been liable for a common injury in general. A right of contribution among tortfeasors tended to promote multiplicity of litigation because it permitted a tortfeasor against whom judgment had been rendered to bring a new and separate suit for contribution against other alleged tortfeasors not named in the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court, which found the statute unconstitutional.

 

1184 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Porter v. Riverside


Civ. No. 8676


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


261 Cal. App. 2d 832; 68 Cal. Rptr. 313; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1811



May 6, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Riverside County. Russell S. Waite, Judge.

Action by a taxpayer to restrain the City of Riverside from paying an expense allowance to city councilmen.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment for plaintiff reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Riverside County (California), which granted plaintiff taxpayer's petition to restrain the city from paying an expense allowance to a city councilmen.


OVERVIEW: The city council adopted an ordinance, Riverside, Cal., Ordinance No. 3300, that fixed each councilman's expense allowance to a certain sum per month but did not require proof of such expenditures. The taxpayer contended that such ordinance was in violation of the city charter, which did not allow the city councilmen to be compensated for their work, even though their expenses could be reimbursed. The court upheld the validity of the ordinance. The court found that the trial court erred when it went behind the ordinance and received evidence aliunde to establish facts that would tend to impeach and overturn the law. The city council, when it passed the ordinance, was presumed to have made a finding of fact that each city councilman's expenses were at least $ 350. The trial court's review should have been confined to a consideration of those facts, which appeared on the face of the ordinance, together with those facts within its judicial knowledge, rather than testimony as to the actual monthly expenditures. If a condition was possible, the court had to assume in favor of the legislative enactment that it existed and was ascertained before the enactment of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1185 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Samson Market Co. v. Kirby


Civ. No. 32647


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


261 Cal. App. 2d 577; 68 Cal. Rptr. 130; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1779



April 26, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitioner's Application for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 19, 1968. Peters, J., and Mosk, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING in mandamus to compel the director of the Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control to extend the time for cancellation of a liquor license.



DISPOSITION: Peremptory writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner business owner brought a proceeding in mandamus to compel respondent, the director of the Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control (California), to extend the time for cancellation of the owner's liquor license for a reasonable period of time after such time as the pending accusations against the license were ultimately determined, or until such time as the Department consented to the transfer of said license to other persons.


OVERVIEW: The owner sought a writ of mandate to compel the director to grant an extension of time under Cal. Admin. Code tit. 4, R. 65 within which the license could be cancelled. The owner argued that a cancellation of its license pursuant to Rule 65(d) would be unconstitutional and in excess of the Department's jurisdiction. In denying the petition, the court found no merit in the owner's contention. The power of the Department to adopt a rule such as Rule 65 was derived from Cal. Const. art. XX, § 22 and Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 25750. The court noted that the power of the Department to adopt rules such as rule 65 and to interpret them could not be questioned, so long as the agency, under the guise of its rule making power, did not abridge or enlarge its authority or exceed the powers given to it by the statute. The court found that in adopting Cal. Admin. Code tit. 4, R. 65 the Department did not exceed the powers given to it, nor did it thereby seek to abridge or enlarge its authority. The court concluded that Rule 65 was constitutional in its opinion and that the owner had not made out a case for judicial interference with the decisions of the Department of which it complained.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition for a peremptory writ of mandate.

 

1186 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Hutton v. Pasadena City Schools


Civ. No. 31205


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


261 Cal. App. 2d 586; 68 Cal. Rptr. 103; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1780



April 26, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Shirley M. Hufstedler, Judge.

Action for declaratory relief to determine whether a school district has the authority to voluntarily pay custodian crewman for the period of time during his suspension and dismissal from employment following his arrest and conviction and prior to a new trial and acquittal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying relief affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff school district employee appealed a judgment of the Los Angeles County Superior Court (California) that denied him declaratory relief and that granted summary judgment to defendant school district on the employee's suit to be paid for time spent while on dismissal. The trial court found that the school district had not adopted the merit pay system and that any back pay to the employee would thus violate Cal. Const. art. IV, §§ 31, 32.


OVERVIEW: A school district employee was convicted of child molestation and dismissed. He did not challenge his dismissal. After a second trial, the employee was acquitted and reinstated. He sought back pay for the time during the dismissal. The court on appeal found that such back pay was impossible because the school district had not adopted any regulations under Cal. Educ. Code § 13601 to allow for such reimbursement. The court further found that the district had not adopted the merit system of employment which would have afforded appellant the relief sought under § 13742. The court held that compensation to the employee without benefit of one of these two authorities would violate the anti-gift provisions of Cal. Const. art. IV, §§ 31, 32. Finally, the court held that the fact that not all school districts were required to adopt a merit system under Cal. Educ. Code § 13742 did not mean that the statute violated Equal Protection because the legislature had presumably found meaningful differences between the various school districts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment awarded to the school district on the employee's declaratory judgment action regarding back pay for time while dismissed from employment.

 

1187 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Barton


Crim. No. 4634


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


261 Cal. App. 2d 561; 68 Cal. Rptr. 157; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1777



April 25, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 19, 1968. Burke, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment (order granting probation) of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. (Albert H. Mundt, Judge.

Prosecution for assault upon a peace officer.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment of conviction reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment from the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which entered a jury verdict finding him guilty of assault upon a peace officer, a violation of Cal. Penal Code § 241, and granted him probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a passenger in an automobile which struck another car, was taken to the hospital for a blood alcohol analysis. In the hospital a struggle broke out between defendant and several highway patrol officers. The officers testified that defendant initiated violence against the officers, but defendant claimed that he had only refused submission to physical force of the blood alcohol test. The court concluded that the jury instruction given by the trial court regarding a defendant's right to refuse a blood alcohol test was improper and reversed. It was apparent that under some circumstances enforced blood withdrawal would evoke the exclusionary rule. Thus, the instruction's blanket rejection of a right of refusal resulted in an incorrect statement of law. Moreover, the court found that the instruction was an abstraction only, not pertinent to the issue before the jury. Finally, the error was prejudicial in that it virtually told the jury that defendant's claim of passive resistance was devoid of constitutional right, depriving it of recognition in law whatever its credibility in fact.


OUTCOME: The court reversed.

 

1188 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Mason


Crim. No. 14523


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


261 Cal. App. 2d 348; 68 Cal. Rptr. 17; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1752



April 19, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied May 14, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Municipal Court of the Whittier Judicial District of Los Angeles County. John L. Donnellan, Judge.

Prosecution for possession of a pinball machine in violation of a municipal ordinance.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment of dismissal after demurrer was sustained reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the decision of the Municipal Court of the Whittier Judicial District of Los Angeles County (California), which sustained defendant's demurrer and entered a judgment dismissing the charge of possession of a pinball machine, pursuant to Santa Fe Springs, Cal., Ordinance 25, §§ 1-6 (1957). Defendant had successfully argued that the state's gambling law, Cal. Penal Code § 330, preempted the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Before the city was incorporated, its residents were subject to a county ordinance that prohibited possession of pinball machines. After incorporation, the county ordinance became inoperative. The city then enacted Santa Fe Springs, Cal., Ordinance 25, §§ 1-6 (1957) to continue the prohibition against pinball machine ownership. Defendant was charged with a misdemeanor under the ordinance; but the municipal court dismissed the charge and held that Cal. Penal Code § 330, which barred games of chance but not of skill, had preempted the ordinance. The state appealed. The court examined the language of the ordinance and of the statute. The court found that the state legislature did not intend to cover the entire field as to regulation of pinball machines. The court explained that the ordinance was a mere supplement to the state law and was not preempted. Whether the pinball machine in this case, however, was predominantly a game of chance or a game of skill was a question of fact. The court reversed and directed the municipal court to allow defendant to replead to the complaint.


OUTCOME: The court held that the state's gambling laws excluding pinball did not preempt the town's power to enact a public ordinance prohibiting pinball machines. Whether the pinball machine was a game of skill permitted under state law or a game of chance prohibited by state law was a question of fact. The court reversed and instructed the municipal court to allow defendant to replead to the complaint.

 

1189 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Rogers v. Centrone


Civ. No. 31660


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


261 Cal. App. 2d 361; 67 Cal. Rptr. 909; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1754



April 19, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Conrad J. Moss, Judge.

Action for damages for personal injuries sustained in a collision with a vehicle driven by a public employee while acting within the scope of his employment.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal after demurrer to first amended complaint sustained without leave to amend affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff accident victim, citing the Due Process and Equal Protection Clauses of the Constitution, appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) dismissing, under Cal. Gov't Code § 950.6, the accident victim's action against defendant driver seeking damages for injuries allegedly sustained when the automobile in which she was riding collided with a vehicle owned by a school district and operated by the driver.


OVERVIEW: The accident victim had brought a companion claim against the school district. The driver contended on appeal that the action was barred by the six-month limitation period of Cal. Gov't Code § 950.6. The accident victim argued that shortening the statute of limitations for suits against public employees to six months rather than the normal one-year limitation period created an arbitrary and unreasonable classification. The court affirmed the judgment. The court noted that the accident victim's action was filed after the expiration of the six-month limitation period. The court stated that the decision of the legislature as to what was a sufficient distinction to warrant a classification would not be overthrown by the courts unless it was palpably arbitrary. The court determined that the statute did not create a class out of a class, but applied to all suits against public employees for damages or injury caused by them while acting within the scope of their employment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the driver in the accident victim's negligence action.

 

1190 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Ambrose v. Cranston


Civ. No. 31141


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


261 Cal. App. 2d 137; 68 Cal. Rptr. 22; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1727



April 15, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 11, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Brodie Ahlport, Judge.

Action for increased retirement benefits under the Judges' Retirement Law.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying relief affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the retired judges and the widows of retired judges, appealed a decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which entered judgment in favor of defendant California State Controller in plaintiffs action for a declaration that they were entitled to increased retirement benefits under the Judges' Retirement Law, Cal. Gov't Code §§ 75000-75109, as amended by Cal. Gov't Code §§ 75075- 75079 (1959).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs retired pursuant to Cal. Gov't Code § 75025, which established the criteria for eligibility for retirement or Cal. Gov't Code § 75060, which provided for disability retirement. The thereby became entitled, under Cal. Gov't Code §§ 75032, 75060.6 to retirement benefits amounting to 50 percent of the current salary of the holder of the office to which they had last been elected. Plaintiffs contended that under a new statutory amendment, Cal. Gov't Code §§ 75075- 75079, they were entitled to higher benefits. The court disagreed. Because plaintiffs ceased to occupy any judicial office when they retired, Cal. Gov't Code § 75002 suggested that the legislature considered them not to be "judges" after retirement. Thus, none of plaintiffs fell within the class described in Cal. Gov't Code § 75075(b). In addition, § 75075 on its face excluded plaintiffs by the phrase "hereafter retiring." The legislature understood "hereafter retiring" to mean retiring after the effective date of the amendment, because only judges so retiring could qualify for receipt of Cal. Gov't Code art. 3.6 benefits by electing, in writing, at or prior to retirement, to receive them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1191 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Chapman


Crim. No. 4665


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


261 Cal. App. 2d 149; 67 Cal. Rptr. 601; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1729



April 15, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied May 13, 1968, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 11, 1968. Mosk, J., did not Participate Therein.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Joaquin County. Robert P. Sullivan, Judge.

Prosecution for first degree murder and first degree robbery.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part. Judgment of conviction affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Joaquin (California) in which defendant was found guilty of first-degree murder and first-degree robbery and was imposed concurrent life sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of first-degree murder and first-degree robbery and was imposed concurrent life sentences. Defendant appealed from the judgment. One issue on appeal was whether defendant's dual sentence violated the proscription against multiple punishment. The court held that when a series of connected crimes was incident to one objective, the defendant could be punished for the most serious offense but not for more than one. Here, the evidence pointed to two acts of robbery; taking of the bar receipts and taking of the victim's personal funds at the scene of the shooting. However, all of defendant's actions were incident to the single objective of robbery, and only one punishment for the more serious crime was permitted. Thus, the court set aside the robbery sentence but affirmed the judgment in all other respects.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the robbery sentence because it held that when a series of conduct crimes was incident to one objective, the defendant could be punished for the most serious offense, but not more than one; judgment was affirmed in all other respects.

 

1192 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lee


Crim. No. 13864


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


260 Cal. App. 2d 836; 67 Cal. Rptr. 709; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1923



April 9, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Edward C. Olson, Judge.

Prosecution for possession of marijuana.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction of unlawfully being in a place where narcotics are used affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted him following a nonjury trial of unlawfully being in a place where narcotics were used with knowledge that such activity was occurring, in violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11556.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a passenger in a car that was stopped because it did not have a front license plate. As the police officers approached the care they smelled marijuana and asked defendant and the driver to get out of the car. The officers observed that defendant's eyes were bloodshot and watery, his pupils were dilated, and his speech was slurred. They arrested defendant, then searched the automobile and found two marijuana cigarettes. Defendant was convicted of unlawfully being in a place where narcotics were used with knowledge that such activity was occurring, in violation of § 11556. On appeal, his conviction was affirmed. The officers had reasonable cause to stop the car because of the missing license plate. They had reasonable cause to arrest defendant based upon their observations of his appearance and behavior. Therefore, the search was incident to the arrest and was valid. There was ample evidence that defendant had knowledge that marijuana was being used as required by § 11556. The court held that an automobile was a "place" within the meaning of § 11556. The court also held that § 11556 was constitutional because it required knowledge that unlawful activity was occurring.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of unlawfully being in a place where narcotics were used.

 

1193 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Agnello


Crim. No. 14417


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


259 Cal. App. 2d 785; 66 Cal. Rptr. 571; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2021



March 4, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the Municipal Court for the Los Angeles Judicial District of Los Angeles County dismissing that count of a complaint which concerned nonstudent conduct at a public educational facility. Michael J. Yelovich, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The prosecution appealed dismissal of a Cal. Penal Code § 602.7 charge against defendant for refusing to obey a university official from the Municipal Court for the Los Angeles Judicial District of Los Angeles County (California), and the question of the constitutionality of this statute for vagueness and ambiguity was certified as an important question of law.


OVERVIEW: The prosecution filed a complaint charging defendant with disturbing the peace and refusing to obey a university official. Defendant demurred to the second charge as unconstitutional for ambiguity and vagueness. The court sustained the demurrer and dismissed the charge. The prosecution appealed, and the appellate court reversed and remanded, certifying the appeal in order to settle an important question of law. On review, the court determined that the charge, pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 602.7, was constitutional. The claim of ambiguity or vagueness on the face of the statute lacked merit, and the section was constitutionally immune from attack. The court saw no uncertainty in the statute that punished defendant's refusal to move upon an order by a university official where the act was likely to interfere with public property. In reversing dismissal of the charge, the court held that § 602.7 did not require the doing of an act in terms so vague that men of common intelligence must necessarily guess at its meaning and differ as to its application.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the charge against defendant for refusing to obey a university official and remanded for further proceedings.

 

1194 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gann


Crim. No. 3009


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


259 Cal. App. 2d 706; 66 Cal. Rptr. 508; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2015



February 29, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied March 19, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Bernardino County. James E. Cunningham, Sr., Judge.

Prosecution for sex perversion and for the infamous crime against nature.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Superior Court of San Bernardino County (California), which convicted him under Cal. Penal Code § 288a of sex perversion and an infamous crime against nature pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 286.


OVERVIEW: During their trial for crimes arising from child molestation, a co-defendant was permitted to proceed in propia persona, and the trial court denied defendant's motion to sever the trials. The court affirmed defendant's convictions under Cal. Penal Code § 288a for sex perversion, and under Cal. Penal Code § 286 for an infamous crime against nature because (1) the information was sufficient under Cal. Penal Code § 952 to provide notice of the crimes of which defendant was accused, (2) pornographic photographs shown to the victims were admissible within the trial court's discretion, (3) defendant was not prejudiced by the co-defendant's proceeding in propia persona without severance of the trial, (4) Cal. Penal Code § 286 was not unconstitutionally vague, and (5) defendant waived the 21-day sentencing requirement of Cal. Penal Code § 1191 by applying for probation, participating in a proceeding under Cal. Welf. and Inst. Code § 5501, and by failing to object to the delay before the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to convict defendant of sex perversion and an infamous crime against nature.

 

1195 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Blevens v. Sfetku


Civ. No. 31168


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


259 Cal. App. 2d 527; 66 Cal. Rptr. 486; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 1996



February 27, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. George A. Dockweiler, Judge.

Action for damages for personal injuries sustained in a water-skiing accident allegedly caused by defendant's negligence in operating a motorboat.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment of nonsuit reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff water-skier (the skier) sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted defendant boat operator's (the operator) motion for nonsuit in a personal injury suit.


OVERVIEW: The skier was injured after the operator made a sudden turn. The skier filed a personal injury suit against the operator, but the trial court granted the operator's motion for nonsuit. On appeal, however, the court reversed the trial court holding that the trial court had erroneously applied Cal. Harb. & Nav. Code § 661.1 to bar the skier's recovery. The court then determined that it had subject matter jurisdiction over the claim pursuant to the saving to suitors clause applicable to maritime actions. The court further held that because § 661.1 barred recovery against the operator because the skier was his guest, it conflicted with 46 U.S.C.S. § 526l of the Motorboat Act. The court also held that although the accident occurred on the forum state's side of an interstate waterway, federal law applied to the skier's claim.


OUTCOME: The court reversed an order of the trial court, which granted the operator's motion for nonsuit in the skier's personal injury suit.

 

1196 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Pacheco


Crim. No. 11658


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


258 Cal. App. 2d 800; 66 Cal. Rptr. 142; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2476



February 13, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied February 23, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Barbara County. W. Preston Butcher, Judge.

Prosecution for burglary, assault with intent to commit rape and assault with a deadly weapon.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction of first degree burglary, assault with intent to commit rape and assault with a deadly weapon affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions for three counts of first degree burglary, three counts of assault with intent to commit rape, and three counts of assault with a deadly weapon. Defendant's convictions were obtained by the state in the Superior Court of Santa Barbara County (California).


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his convictions for burglary, assault with intent to commit rape, and assault with a deadly weapon. On appeal, the court held that each victim named in the indictment was able to identify appellant, either visually or by his voice, each was threatened by a screwdriver, and the circumstances of each offense were similar in several other respects. The court held that there was a definite behavior pattern in appellant's criminal modus operandi and such testimony was admissible for that purpose. Appellant also challenged the constitutionality of Cal. Penal Code §§ 1367 and 1368, claiming that the statutes contravened the Fifth Amendment privilege against self-incrimination. The court held that none of the statements appellant made to his psychiatrists were received in evidence at the trial which commenced more than one month after the final proceeding under §§ 1367 and 1368. Therefore there was no merit to his claim.


OUTCOME: The court ruled in favor of the state and affirmed appellant's convictions for burglary, assault with intent to commit rape, and assault with a deadly weapon.

 

1197 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Johnson


Crim. No. 2628


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


258 Cal. App. 2d 705; 66 Cal. Rptr. 99; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2466



February 7, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied April 4, 1968. Mosk, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. William A. Glen, Judge.

Prosecution for a father's failure to provide for his minor children and remaining out of the state for more than 30 days during such failure.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment of conviction reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California) convicting him of failing to provide for his minor children and remaining out of the state for a period in excess of 30 days during such failure, entered upon a jury verdict.


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of the crime of failing to provide for minor children as charged in the information. The court held that because the information not only charged defendant with failing to provide, but also with remaining out of the state for a period of more than 30 days while failing to provide, the trial court committed prejudicial error in omitting from its instruction the essential fact of absence from the state. The propriety of the instruction, which directed the jury to find defendant guilty if certain facts were found to be true beyond a reasonable doubt, depended upon its including all of the legal elements essential to the verdict. The court also held that (1) the presumption of Cal. Penal Code § 270 that a father was outside the state when he failed to provide for his children for more than 30 days violated due process and was unconstitutional, (2) the trial court erred in instructing on the father's refusal to comply with a support order for more than 10 days, without evidence of when the order was made, and (3) the trial court erred in failing to instruct on the lesser included misdemeanor offense of failing to provide for minor children.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the case for a new trial and for such further proceedings as might be appropriate.

 

1198 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Hofberg v. County of Los Angeles Civil Service Com.


Civ. No. 24242


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Four


258 Cal. App. 2d 433; 65 Cal. Rptr. 759; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2429



January 31, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Alfred Gitelson, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the Civil Service Commission to certify plaintiff's eligibility for appointment as a social worker.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment granting writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Civil Service Commission of the County of Los Angeles (California) sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted appellee employee's request for a writ mandating that the Commission was to certify him as being eligible for appointment as a social worker for the county.


OVERVIEW: The employee had previously been discharged from county employment because, during his appearance before the House of Representatives Committee on Un-American Activities, he asserted his Fifth Amendment privilege and refused to answer questions under Cal. Gov't. Code § 1028.1, relating to his loyalty to the government. The employee later passed an exam for employment as a social worker, however, the Commission withheld his name from the eligible list because it deemed his work history unsatisfactory. The employee appealed, asserting that he would answer any question under § 1028.1 propounded by the Commission. The decision was affirmed without a hearing or providing any facts. On appeal, the court held that the trial court properly concluded that the Commission's refusal to certify him as an employee without a hearing was arbitrary and unreasonable. The court noted that the Committee was not permitted to bar the employee from county work for arbitrary reasons. The court concluded that because the employee repeatedly informed the Commission that he would answer any questions asked of him relating to his loyalty or subversive activities, there was no reason to refuse certification.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment granting the writ.

 

1199 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Parrish v. Municipal Court for Modesto Judicial Dist.


Civ. No. 793


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


258 Cal. App. 2d 497; 65 Cal. Rptr. 862; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2437



January 31, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 28, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Stanislaus County. Robert D. Carter, Judge.

Proceeding in prohibition to forbid the Municipal Court of the Modesto Judicial District from prosecuting a defendant any further for the violation of Pen. Code, § 602, subd. (o).



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment granting writ reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant municipal court sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Stanislaus County (California), which granted respondent trespasser's writ and prohibited the municipal court from prosecuting the trespasser for criminal trespass in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 602(o).


OVERVIEW: The trespasser refused to leave a county welfare office until the officials agreed to provide assistance to an impoverished family. The officials refused to agree to the trespasser's demands. He remained in the building after hours and after he was asked to leave. He was arrested and charged with a violation of Cal. Penal Code § 602(o). The trespasser filed a writ to prohibit the municipal court from prosecuting the case. The trial court granted the writ and permanently stayed all further proceedings. On appeal, the court reversed. The court concluded that the law was properly enforceable for the protection of the county's buildings and to carry out public business. The fact that county officials did not see fit to request the trespasser to leave the building on a prior occasion did not give the trespasser a right to repeat his actions and to fail to comply with the law. The fact that the trespasser was a good deed for the benefit of a needy family did not excuse a breach of the law.


OUTCOME: The court ruled in favor of the municipal court and against the trespasser and reversed the judgment. The court directed the trial court to set aside the writ of prohibition.

 

1200 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


San Carlos School Dist. v. State Board of Education


Civ. No. 24308


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


258 Cal. App. 2d 317; 65 Cal. Rptr. 711; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2417



January 26, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Mateo County. Melvin E. Cohn, Judge.

Action by a school district seeking injunction and writ of mandate against the State Board of Education and seeking to have the Unruh School Act declared unconstitutional.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal on failure to amend after demurrer to complaint sustained with leave to amend, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school district sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California), which dismissed the school district's complaint that sought an injunction and writ of mandate against respondent State Board of Education (board). The school district also sought to have the Unruh School Act of 1964 (Act), 1965 Cal. Stat. ch. 132 (First Executive Session 1966) declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The school district sought a writ of mandamus and in effect charged the board with an abuse of discretion in rejecting a locally formulated plan for school district reorganization and in submitting a plan devised by the board to the electorate in lieu thereof. The school district also challenged the constitutionality of the Act, which altered school district boundaries and the disposition of district funds. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that: (1) the school district had sufficient standing to challenge the constitutionality of legislation, which the school district contended directly affected its boundaries, its property, and its funds; (2) the transfer of the property of one district to another district did not constitute a taking of property without due process of law because the legislature had plenary power over school districts; (3) Cal. Educ. Code § 17676 did not violate Cal. Const. art. I, § 21 because the statute operated uniformly throughout the entire state and benefited every district that was similarly situated by voting for unification; and (4) Cal. Educ. Code § 17676 did not violate Cal. Const. art. XX, § 11 because no district or elector was coerced.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment dismissing the school district's complaint that sought an injunction and writ of mandate against the board and to have the Act declared unconstitutional.
